Weight Standard of the Dirham and Mithqal in Zakat
Definition of weight standards for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the authoritative weight of the dirham (14 qirats) and mithqal (20 qirats), perform conversions between them, and understand the impact on zakat calculation.

Core Idea
The Hanafi dirham is 14 qirats; the mithqal is 20 qirats; adding 3/7 of a dirham yields a mithqal.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira establishes the weight standard for the silver dirham and the gold mithqal, both crucial for determining nisab in zakat. The dirham is fixed at 14 qirats, the mithqal at 20 qirats, with a precise conversion formula. Understanding these weights ensures accurate zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Learn the base units
The dirham weighs 14 qirats; the mithqal weighs 20 qirats. These are fixed standards.
1 qirat is a small unit of weight, 1/20 of a mithqal.
2
Understand conversion from dirham to mithqal
To convert dirhams to mithqals, add 3/7 of the dirham's weight. For example, 1 dirham + 3/7 dirham = 10/7 dirham ≈ 1.4286 dirhams = 1 mithqal.
This works because 1 dirham = 14 qirats, and 3/7 of 14 = 6 qirats, adding to 20 qirats.
3
Understand conversion from mithqal to dirham
To convert mithqals to dirhams, subtract 3/10 of the mithqal (which is 6 qirats). For example, 1 mithqal - 3/10 mithqal = 7/10 mithqal = 14 qirats = 1 dirham.
3/10 of 20 qirats is 6 qirats.
4
Apply to zakat nisab
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams, each of 14 qirats. For gold, the nisab is 20 mithqals. Understanding weights allows correct calculation of nisab in different measures.
This is essential for practical zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الفضة
ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعين درهماً، فيكون فيها درهم.
ثم في كل أربعين درهماً : درهم عند أبي حنيفة .
وقالا : ما زاد على المائتين : فزكاته بحسابها .
وعشرون مثقالاً: فثلثه سبعة.
وقال محمد بن الفضل : المعتبر في كل زمان بدرهمه، وبه أفتى جماعة من المتأخرين ، إلا أن الأول هو المعتبر، وهو أربعة عشر قيراطاً،
وعليه إطباق كتب المتقدمين والمتأخرين، وهو الأظهر. واعلم أنك متى زدت على الدرهم ثلاثة أسباعه، مثقالاً؛ لأن المثقال عشرون قيراطاً، ومتى نقصت من المثقال ثلاثة أعشاره وهي ستة : كان درهماً؛ لأن الدرهم أربعة عشر قيراطاً. قوله: (ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعين درهماً، فيكون فيها درهم مع الخمسة، ثم في كل أربعين درهماً درهم عند أبي حنيفة). * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: ما زاد على المائتين: فزكاته بحسابه)، قلت الزيادة أو كثرت حتى لو كانت الزيادة درهماً : ففيه جزء من أربعين جزءاً من درهم، وهو ربع عشره.
Chapter of Zakat of Silver. And there is nothing in the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then in it is one dirham. Then in every forty dirhams: one dirham according to Abu Hanifa. And they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: What exceeds two hundred, its zakat is in proportion to it. And twenty mithqals: its third is seven. And Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: The standard in every time is its dirham, and a group of later scholars gave fatwa accordingly, except that the first is the standard, which is fourteen qirats, and upon it is the agreement of the books of the earlier and later scholars, and it is the most apparent. And know that whenever you add to the dirham three sevenths of it, it becomes a mithqal; because the mithqal is twenty qirats, and whenever you subtract from the mithqal three tenths of it, which are six, it becomes a dirham; because the dirham is fourteen qirats. His saying: (And there is nothing in the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then in it is one dirham with the five, then in every forty dirhams one dirham according to Abu Hanifa). * His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: What exceeds two hundred, its zakat is in proportion to it), I say: whether the increase is small or large, even if the increase were one dirham, then in it is a part of forty parts of a dirham, which is one fortieth (literally a quarter of its tenth).
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on zakat of silver. The matn states that no zakat is due on silver until it reaches 40 dirhams (nisab), then 1 dirham is due. For every additional 40 dirhams, 1 dirham is due according to Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the two disciples (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that for amounts exceeding 200 dirhams, the zakat is calculated proportionally (i.e., 1/40 of the excess). This is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage then discusses the weight of the dirham relative to the mithqal (gold coin). The standard dirham is 14 qirats, while the mithqal is 20 qirats. Thus, 7 dirhams equal 5 mithqals (since 7*14=98, 5*20=100, approximate), and the text shows the conversion: adding 3/7 of a dirham gives a mithqal. The preferred weight standard is 14 qirats per dirham. The commentary also reiterates the nisab and the dispute.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin of a specific weight, here standardized at 14 qirats.
مثقال (mithqal): A gold coin of 20 qirats weight.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1 qirat = 1/20 of a mithqal or 1/14 of a dirham.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many dirhams are equivalent to 56 qirats?
A) 4
B) 5
C) 3
D) 2

Key Takeaway
The dirham weight of 14 qirats determines the silver nisab; accurate conversion between dirham and mithqal is essential for zakat.

Zakat on Mixed Coins: The Dominance Rule
Ruling on coins containing alloy based on dominant metal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for mixed silver/gold coins to determine whether zakat is due on total weight, as a trade good, or on the extracted pure metal.

Core Idea
The ruling of a mixed coin follows its dominant metal; if the alloy dominates, it becomes a trade good.

This lesson examines how Hanafi fiqh categorizes coins that contain both pure metal and alloy (ghish). The central principle is that the ruling depends on which component is predominant. When the pure metal (silver or gold) is the majority, the coin is treated as pure, and zakat is calculated on its total weight. When the alloy is the majority, the coin is removed from the ruling of its metal and treated as a trade good (urud), subject to zakat on its market value—provided the owner had trade intention. The text also introduces a physical test (burning) to determine if a nisab of pure metal can be extracted, and reports three opinions for when the two components are equal.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases covered in the passage: (a) majority pure metal, (b) majority alloy, (c) equal mixture.
These are the only cases; the text does not consider a scenario where both are equal in a different proportion.
2
2. Rule for majority pure metal
When silver or gold is predominant, the alloy is considered 'consumed' (mustahlik) and ignored. The coin is treated as pure, so zakat is wajib on its total weight if it reaches nisab.
No need to calculate the pure metal separately; the entire weight counts.
3
3. Rule for majority alloy
When the alloy dominates, the coin is no longer in the ruling of silver/gold. It becomes a trade good. Zakat is due at 1/40 of its market value, provided that value reaches a nisab and the owner had trade intention (niyyat al-tijarah).
The text also adds: if burning can extract a nisab of pure metal, then zakat on that pure metal takes precedence.
4
4. Analyze the proof (dalil)
The evidence for treating an alloy-dominant coin as a trade good is that it can be sold for silver with disparity (mufadalah). Pure silver cannot be sold for silver with disparity (riba). This qiyas shows the coin is not in the ruling of silver.
The proof is aqli (rational) based on the prohibition of riba.
5
5. Equal mixture: three opinions
When pure and alloy are equal, later scholars differ: some say zakat on full weight (precaution), some say half, some say nothing. The text does not give a preference.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. A mufti would need to consider the tarjih of later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإذا كان الغالب على الوَرِق: الفضة: فهي في حكم الفضة)؛ لأنها إذا كانت هي الغالبة : كان الغش مستهلكاً، فلا اعتبار به، وإذا كان الغالب على الدنانير الذهب : فهو في حُكْمِ الذهب . وإذا كان الغالب عليها الغش : فهي في حُكم العُروض، يُعتبر أن تبلغ قيمتها نصاباً . وهو أن تكون الفضة زائدة على النصف، وإن كان الغالب على الدنانير الذهب: فهو في حكم الذهب). قوله: (وإذا كان الغالب عليها الغش فهي في حكم العروض)؛ لأن غلبته عليها: يُخرجها عن حكم الفضة، بدليل جواز بيعها بالفضة متفاضلاً. وإنما تكون في حكم العروض إذا كانت بحال لو أُحرقت: لا يخلص منها نصاب، أما إذا كان يخلص منها نصاب: وجب زكاة الخالص. وإذا استوى الخالص والغش: قال في الينابيع»: اختلف فيه المتأخرون على ثلاثة أقوال: قال بعضهم: يجب خمسة؛ احتياطاً، وقال بعضهم: درهمان ونصف، وقال بعضهم: لا يجب شيء. * قوله: (ويعتبر أن تبلغ قيمتها نصاباً). ولا بد فيه من نية التجارة، كسائر العروض.
His saying: (And if the majority of the silver coin is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver); because if it is the majority, the alloy is considered consumed, so it is not considered. And if the majority of the gold dinars is gold, then it is in the ruling of gold. And if the majority is alloy, then it is in the ruling of trade goods, and it is considered that its value reaches a nisab. That is, that the silver be in excess of the half, and if the majority of the dinars is gold, then it is in the ruling of gold). His saying: (And if the majority is alloy, then it is in the ruling of trade goods); because its preponderance over it takes it out of the ruling of silver, as evidenced by the permissibility of selling it for silver with disparity. And it is in the ruling of trade goods only if it is such that if it were burned, a nisab would not be extracted from it. But if a nisab would be extracted from it, then the zakat of the pure (metal) is obligatory. And if the pure and the alloy are equal: It is said in al-Yanabi' that the later scholars differed on three opinions: Some said: five (dirhams) must be given as a precaution; some said: two and a half dirhams; and some said: nothing is due. * His saying: (And it is considered that its value reaches a nisab). And it is necessary to have the intention of trade, as with other trade goods.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage addresses the zakat on coins that contain a mixture of pure metal and alloy (ghish). The ruling depends on which component predominates. If the silver (or gold) is the majority, the coin is treated as pure silver (or gold) and its zakat is calculated based on its total weight, ignoring the alloy (which is 'consumed'). If the alloy is the majority, the coin is treated as a trade good (urud), meaning its market value is considered, and if that value reaches the nisab of silver, zakat is due at 1/40 of that value, but with the condition that the owner had the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah). The text provides a proof for the latter: it is permissible to sell such a coin for silver with disparity (mufadalah), which is not allowed for pure silver (because selling silver for silver must be equal weight for weight). This indicates the coin is not in the ruling of silver. Additionally, the passage introduces a physical test: if the coin is melted and a nisab of pure metal can be extracted, then zakat is due on the pure metal. If not, it is a trade good. In the case where the pure and alloy are equal, there is no definitive ruling in the text; it only reports three opinions from later scholars: one obligates zakat on the full weight (five dirhams presumably for a 200 dirham coin? actually five is unclear), another says half (2.5 dirhams), and a third says nothing. The text does not choose among them. Finally, the requirement of trade intention is emphasized for the trade good status.

Key Terms
الغش (al-ghish): The alloy or impurity mixed with pure metal in a coin.
العروض (al-'urud): Trade goods, i.e., commodities intended for sale, as opposed to monetary coins.
نية التجارة (niyyat al-tijarah): The intention to use the item for trade when acquiring it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a silver coin contains more alloy than silver, how is zakat calculated?
A) Treated as pure silver based on total weight
B) Treated as a trade good; its market value must reach nisab
C) No zakat is due
D) Treated as gold

Key Takeaway
The dominance of pure metal or alloy determines whether a mixed coin is subject to zakat on weight or as a trade good; equal mixture remains unresolved.

Zakat on Mixed Silver Coins: The Rule of the Majority
Defines zakat treatment of mixed silver coins based on majority component.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the zakat category of a mixed silver coin based on its predominant metal component, apply the exception for extractable pure silver, and identify the ikhtilaf among later Hanafi scholars when silver and alloy are equal.

Core Idea
The majority component of a coin determines its zakat category; alloy dominance shifts it to trade goods.

Early Islamic coins were often mixed with other metals. Knowing how to evaluate them for zakat is essential, as the ruling depends on the predominant content. This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with commentary from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, sets out the Hanafi rule: if silver is the majority, it is treated as silver; if alloy is the majority, it becomes a trade good. There is also an important exception when pure silver can be extracted to nisab, and an ikhtilaf among later scholars when the two components are exactly equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage states that the predominant component (ghālib) determines whether the coin is treated as silver or as a trade good. 'Predominant' means more than half the weight.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Apply the Rule: Alloy Majority
If the alloy content exceeds the pure silver, the coin is removed from the ruling of silver and treated like other trade goods (ʿurūḍ). Evidence: it is permissible to sell such coins for pure silver with disparity (tafadul), which is not allowed for pure silver due to riba.
The proof is a form of istihsan based on common practice.
3
Recognize the Exception: Extractable Pure Silver
If melting the coins would yield a nisab of pure silver, then zakat on that pure silver is wajib, even if the alloy is the majority by weight. The coin is only treated as a trade good when no nisab can be extracted.
This exception overrides the usual majority rule.
4
Analyze the Equal Case
When pure silver and alloy are exactly equal in weight, later scholars (mutakhkhirūn) differed: some said five dirhams (precaution), some said two and a half dirhams, and some said no zakat is due.
The text does not specify which opinion is muftā bihī.
5
Confirm Conditions for Trade Goods
When a coin is treated as a trade good, zakat is only wajib if its total market value reaches the nisab (of gold or silver) and the owner has the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijāra).
This is the same condition as for any other merchandise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الفضة
وإذا كان الغالب على الدنانير الذهب : فهو في حُكْمِ الذهب . وإذا كان الغالب عليها الغش : فهي في حُكم العُروض، يُعتبر أن تبلغ قيمتها نصاباً .
وهو أن تكون الفضة زائدة على النصف، وإن كان الغالب على الدنانير الذهب: فهو في حكم الذهب).
قوله: (وإذا كان الغالب عليها الغش فهي في حكم العروض)؛ لأن غلبته عليها: يُخرجها عن حكم الفضة، بدليل جواز بيعها بالفضة متفاضلاً.
وإنما تكون في حكم العروض إذا كانت بحال لو أُحرقت: لا يخلص منها نصاب، أما إذا كان يخلص منها نصاب: وجب زكاة الخالص.
وإذا استوى الخالص والغش:
قال في الينابيع»: اختلف فيه المتأخرون على ثلاثة أقوال: قال بعضهم: يجب خمسة؛ احتياطاً، وقال بعضهم: درهمان ونصف، وقال بعضهم: لا يجب شيء.
* قوله: (ويعتبر أن تبلغ قيمتها نصاباً).
ولا بد فيه من نية التجارة، كسائر العروض.
Chapter on Zakat of Silver. If the majority of dinars is gold, then it is in the ruling of gold. And if the majority upon them is alloy, then they are in the ruling of trade goods, and it is considered that their value reaches the nisab. And that is that the silver exceeds half, and if the majority of dinars is gold, then it is in the ruling of gold. His saying: (And if the majority upon them is alloy then they are in the ruling of trade goods); because its predominance over them removes them from the ruling of silver, as evidenced by the permissibility of selling them for silver with disparity. And they are only in the ruling of trade goods if they are in a state such that if they were melted, no nisab of pure [silver] would come out. But if a nisab of pure [silver] would come out, then zakat on the pure is obligatory. And if the pure and alloy are equal: He said in al-Yanabi': the later scholars differed on three opinions: some said: five [dirhams] are obligatory, as a precaution; some said: two and a half dirhams; and some said: nothing is obligatory. * His saying: (And it is considered that its value reaches the nisab). And intention of trade is necessary in it, like other trade goods.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the zakat of silver coins that are mixed with other metals. It opens with the general rule: the predominant component determines the ruling. If a dinar (gold coin) is predominantly gold, it is treated as gold. If a silver coin is predominantly alloy (ghish), it is treated as trade goods, meaning zakat is due only if its value reaches the nisab and there is intention of trade. The commentator then clarifies that 'predominant' means the pure silver must exceed half. The proof is that such coins can be sold for silver with disparity (tafadul), which is impermissible for pure silver, indicating they are not pure silver. However, if pure silver can be extracted to the amount of nisab by melting, then zakat on the pure silver alone is obligatory. For equal proportions, later scholars differ: some require a precautionary amount of five dirhams, others two and a half, and some nothing. Finally, when treating as trade goods, both value nisab and trade intention are required.

Key Terms
غالب (ghālib): The component that exceeds half of the coin's total weight.
غش (ghish): Alloy, the non-silver or non-gold metal mixed into a coin.
عروض (ʿurūḍ): Trade goods (merchandise) subject to zakat only if they reach nisab by value and are intended for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a silver coin has equal amounts of pure silver and alloy, which of the following is true according to the passage?
A) Zakat must be paid as silver.
B) It is treated as a trade good.
C) Later scholars differed; some say five dirhams, some two and a half, some nothing.
D) No zakat is due under any circumstance.

Key Takeaway
The majority component determines the zakat category of mixed coins, with an exception for extractable pure silver and ikhtilaf when proportions are equal.

Zakat on Gold: Nisab and Rate
Ruling on zakat of gold with nisab and calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of gold in the Hanafi school and calculate the zakat due when the surplus reaches the threshold of 4 mithqal.

Core Idea
Gold zakat: 2.5% due on 20 mithqal and on every additional 4 mithqal.

This lesson covers the foundational rules of zakat on gold in the Hanafi school. You will learn the minimum threshold (nisab), the rate, and how to handle surplus amounts. The passage also explains the reasoning behind the calculation, linking it to the quarter-of-a-tenth principle and the equivalence between gold and silver weights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (zakat on gold) and its hukm level. In the Hanafi school, it is wajib when conditions are met.
Zakat is a financial worship, obligatory on specific assets.
2
State the nisab
Identify the minimum amount that triggers zakat: 20 mithqal (each mithqal = 20 qirat, approx. 85 grams).
The nisab for gold is fixed by hadith.
3
Calculate the amount due
For the nisab, due is half a mithqal (quarter of a tenth). For any excess, no zakat until the excess reaches 4 mithqal, then 2 qirat due.
The calculation uses the quarter-of-a-tenth rate (2.5%).
4
Understand the proof
The dalil is the hadith 'There is no zakat in less than twenty mithqal.' The rate is derived from the general rule of quarter of a tenth.
The proof is a specific text with general application.
5
Note the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that gold has its own nisab and surplus threshold; gold and silver are not combined.
This is contrasted with other schools that may combine or have different thresholds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الذهب
من الذهب صدقة. ليس فيما دون عشرين مثقالاً .
فإذا كانت عشرين مثقالاً، وحالَ عليها الحولُ : ففيها نصف مثقال .
ثم في كل أربعة مثاقيل : قيراطان .
وليس فيما دون أربعة مثاقيل صدقة عند أبي حنيفة،
قال رحمه الله :
باب زكاة الذهب
۱۹۷
: ليس فيما دون عشرين مثقالاً
صدقة، الذهب : من
فإذا كانت عشرين مثقالاً)،
زنة كل مثقال منها: عشرون قيراطاً، (وحال
عليها الحولُ: ففيها نصف مثقال).
قال بعض العلماء في ذلك نظماً:
والفرضُ في عشرين مثقالاً ذهب نصفُ من المثقال في الحول وَجَبْ * (ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعة مثاقيل: فيكون فيها قيراطان)؛ لأن الواجب ربع العشر، والأربعة المثاقيل: ثمانون قيراطاً، وربع عشرها : قيراطان.
وقد اعتبر الشرع كل دينار بعشرة دراهم، فيكون أربعة مثاقيل: كأربعين درهما، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة).
Chapter on Zakat of Gold. From gold is charity. There is nothing in less than twenty mithqals. And if it is twenty mithqals, and a year passes over it, then in it is half a mithqal. Then in every four mithqals: two qirats. And there is nothing in less than four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. The text: Chapter on Zakat of Gold 197: There is nothing in less than twenty mithqals as charity. From gold: if it is twenty mithqals, the weight of each mithqal is twenty qirats, and a year passes over it, then in it is half a mithqal. Some scholars composed poetry: 'The obligatory in twenty mithqals of gold is half a mithqal in the year, it became obligatory. And nothing on the increase until it reaches four mithqals: then in it are two qirats.' Because the obligatory is a quarter of a tenth, and four mithqals is eighty qirats, and a quarter of a tenth of it is two qirats. And the Law has considered each dinar as ten dirhams, so four mithqals are like forty dirhams, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the zakat of gold. It begins with the matn: the nisab for gold is 20 mithqal (each mithqal = 20 qirat). The due amount is half a mithqal (i.e., 2.5 mithqal per year? Actually half a mithqal is exactly 1/40 of 20, which is a quarter of a tenth). For any increase above 20, no zakat is due until the increase reaches 4 mithqal, at which point 2 qirat are due. This is only according to Abu Hanifa. The commentator then explains the calculation: the obligatory rate is a quarter of a tenth (2.5%). For 4 mithqal (80 qirat), a quarter of a tenth is 2 qirat. This is consistent with the equivalence of 1 dinar = 10 dirhams, so 4 mithqal = 40 dirhams, which is the nisab for silver. Abu Hanifa's position is that gold has its own nisab and rate. The poetic lines summarize the rule.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqāl): A unit of weight for gold; 1 mithqal = 20 qirat (approx. 4.25 grams).
قيراط (qīrāṭ): A subdivision of a mithqal; 1 mithqal = 20 qirat. Also a unit of measure for zakat amounts.
ربع العشر (rubʿ al-ʿushr): One quarter of a tenth, i.e., 2.5%, the standard zakat rate on gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how much zakat is due on 23 mithqal of gold after one year?
A) Half a mithqal plus 2 qirat
B) Half a mithqal
C) Quarter of a tenth of 23 mithqal
D) 3 qirat

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold is wajib on 20 mithqal (half mithqal due) and on each subsequent 4 mithqal increment (2 qirat due).

Gold Zakat Nisab and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Increase
Intra-Hanafi ruling and reasoning on gold zakat increment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for gold zakat according to Imam Abu Hanifa and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether zakat is due on an increase below four mithqal.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: no zakat on excess gold until it reaches four mithqal; the Sahibayn: zakat on any excess proportionally.

Zakat on gold is obligatory when the nisab of twenty mithqal (approx. 85 grams) is reached and a lunar year passes. The rate is 2.5% (half a mithqal). But what if you have extra gold beyond the nisab, e.g., 22 mithqal? Must that extra 2 mithqal also be zakatable? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa sets a minimum increment of four mithqal before zakat is due on the excess, while his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that any excess should be zakatable at the same proportional rate. In this passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, the author presents the dispute and explains Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning, anchoring it in the analogy to silver zakat increments.

Guided Path
1
Establish the base nisab
Identify the minimum amount of gold that triggers zakat (20 mithqal) and the rate (half mithqal per 20 mithqal = 2.5%). Understand that each mithqal is 20 qirat.
The nisab is twenty mithqal (approx. 85 g). Rate: half mithqal per twenty, i.e., 1/40 = 2.5%.
2
Identify the dispute on increase
Note that Abu Hanifa says no zakat on the increase until it reaches four mithqal; then for each four mithqal, two qirat (1/40 of four mithqal, i.e., 2.5%) are due. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say zakat is due on any increase over twenty mithqal proportionally.
The dispute is about the threshold: absolute increment of four mithqal (Abu Hanifa) vs. continuous proportion (Sahibayn).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
The text explains that the obligatory is one quarter of one tenth (2.5%). Four mithqal = 80 qirat. 1/40 of 80 qirat = 2 qirat. This matches the rate. Moreover, the Lawgiver equated one dinar (gold) to ten dirhams (silver), so four mithqal gold = forty dirhams silver, which is the increment threshold for silver zakat. Hence analogical reasoning (qiyas) on silver.
This qiyas is the core of Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Contrast the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn see no need for a separate increment nisab. They analogize gold to other zakatable wealth (cash, trade goods) where any increase above the nisab is immediately zakatable at the same rate.
The practical result: on 22 mithqal, Abu Hanifa exempts the extra 2, Sahibayn require zakat on all 22 at 2.5%.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The Hanafi school, especially in later fatwa works, adopts Abu Hanifa's view as the mufta bihi. This is the position to follow in practice.
The commentary does not explicitly choose but presents Abu Hanifa's view as the established one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الذهب: من الذهب صدقة. ليس فيما دون عشرين مثقالاً. فإذا كانت عشرين مثقالاً، وحال عليها الحول: ففيها نصف مثقال. ثم في كل أربعة مثاقيل: قيراطان. وليس فيما دون أربعة مثاقيل صدقة عند أبي حنيفة. قال رحمه الله: باب زكاة الذهب: ليس فيما دون عشرين مثقالاً صدقة، الذهب: من ... فإذا كانت عشرين مثقالاً، زنة كل مثقال منها: عشرون قيراطاً، وحال عليها الحول: ففيها نصف مثقال. قال بعض العلماء في ذلك نظماً: والفرض في عشرين مثقالاً ذهب نصف من المثقال في الحول وجب. ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعة مثاقيل: فيكون فيها قيراطان؛ لأن الواجب ربع العشر، والأربعة المثاقيل: ثمانون قيراطاً، وربع عشرها: قيراطان. وقد اعتبر الشرع كل دينار بعشرة دراهم، فيكون أربعة مثاقيل: كأربعين درهما، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة. وقالا: ما زاد على العشرين: فزكاته بحسابها. وعندهما: تجب في الزيادة على العشرين بحساب ذلك.
Chapter of Zakat of Gold: From gold is charity. There is nothing on less than twenty mithqal. When it reaches twenty mithqal and a year passes over it, then on it is half a mithqal. Then for every four mithqal, two qirat. And there is no charity on less than four mithqal according to Abu Hanifa. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: Chapter of Zakat of Gold: There is no charity on less than twenty mithqal; gold: from... When it is twenty mithqal, the weight of each mithqal is twenty qirat, and a year passes over it, then on it is half a mithqal. Some scholars said in poetry: The obligatory on twenty mithqal of gold is half a mithqal, obligatory in the year. And nothing on the increase until it reaches four mithqal: then on it is two qirat; because the obligatory is one-quarter of one-tenth, and four mithqal are eighty qirat, and one-quarter of their one-tenth is two qirat. And the Lawgiver considered each dinar equal to ten dirhams, so four mithqal are like forty dirhams, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And the two (companions) said: What exceeds twenty: its zakat is by its calculation. And according to them: zakat is due on the increase over twenty by its calculation.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on gold exceeding the nisab. The matn first states the basic ruling: gold zakat is obligatory on a nisab of twenty mithqal (each mithqal = 20 qirat, so 20 mithqal = 400 qirat). The rate is 2.5%: half mithqal on twenty, which equals 2.5% (since 0.5/20=1/40). Then for every additional four mithqal, the zakat is two qirat, which is also 2.5% (since two qirat = 1/10 of a mithqal? Actually 2 qirat = 1/10 of a mithqal? Wait: 1 mithqal = 20 qirat, so 4 mithqal = 80 qirat. 2 qirat is 2/80=1/40). So it's consistent. Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on the increase until it reaches four mithqal, because the nisab for additional gold is measured in increments of four mithqal (similar to the silver nisab of forty dirhams for the initial nisab? Actually for silver the nisab is 200 dirhams, and increase is per 40 dirhams). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that zakat is due on any excess above twenty proportionally, even if it is less than four mithqal. The commentary provides reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view: the obligatory is one-quarter of one-tenth (i.e., 2.5%), and four mithqal (80 qirat) multiplied by 2.5% gives 2 qirat. The text also notes the legal equivalence: one dinar (gold) equals ten dirhams (silver), so four mithqal gold corresponds to forty dirhams silver, which is the nisab increment for silver. Thus Abu Hanifa analogizes gold to silver in terms of the increment threshold. The poem reinforces the ruling.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold; each mithqal equals 20 qirat (about 4.25 grams). The nisab for gold is twenty mithqal.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1/20 of a mithqal. Also used to denote the zakat amount: 2 qirat per 4 mithqal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A hadith stating zakat is due on every mithqal.
B) The analogy to silver zakat increments and the legal equivalence of dinar to dirham.
C) The unanimous consensus of the Companions.
D) The Sahibayn explicitly agreed with him.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat on gold in excess of the nisab is not due until the excess reaches four mithqal, following Imam Abu Hanifa's qiyas on silver increments.

Zakat on Gold and Silver Jewelry: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on zakat for gold/silver jewelry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for gold/silver jewelry, identify the Shafi'i counterposition, and evaluate the Hanafi proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Gold and silver jewelry is zakatable in Hanafi law, even if worn, based on the Prophet's command.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that zakat is due on all forms of gold and silver, including jewelry and utensils, and addresses a well-known Shafi'i objection that jewelry prepared for permissible wear is exempt. The Hanafi school relies on a direct hadith to prove its position. Understanding this dispute highlights how different usul principles lead to different fiqh rulings on a common financial obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the zakatable forms
From the matn, list the three categories of gold/silver that are subject to zakat: raw metal (tibr), jewelry (huly), and utensils (aniyah).
These are all forms of gold/silver, not coins.
2
State the Shafi'i exception
Al-Shafi'i exempts jewelry prepared for permissible use. Understand the rationale: it is akin to personal necessities.
This exception applies only to jewelry, not to tibr or utensils.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Read the hadith of the two women with gold bracelets. Identify the imperative 'addu zakat' as the key evidence. The Prophet (ﷺ) directly commanded zakat on adornment jewelry.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i; its chain is hasan.
4
Apply the ruling to non-metal jewelry
Note that rubies, pearls, and jewels are exempt unless held for trade. This confirms the rule: zakat applies only to gold and silver, not to other precious materials.
This exception reinforces that the basis for zakat is the substance (gold/silver), not the form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي تبر الذهب والفضة وحليهما والآنية منهما الزكاة. التبر: القطعة التي أخرجت من المعدن، وهو غير المضروب. وقوله: وحليهما: قال الشافعي: كل حلي معد للباس المباح: لا تجب فيه الزكاة. لنا: ما روي أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام رأى امرأتين تطوفان، وعليهما سواران من ذهب فقال: أتؤديان زكاتهما؟ قالتا: لا. قال: أتحبان أن يسوركما الله بسوارين من نار جهنم؟ فقالتا: لا، قال: فأديا زكاتهما. وأما اليواقيت واللآلئ والجواهر فلا زكاة فيها وإن كانت حلياً، إلا أن تكون للتجارة.
And on unfabricated gold and silver, their jewelry, and utensils made from them: zakat is due. Al-tibr: the piece that is taken from the mine, and it is not minted. And his words: and their jewelry: al-Shafi'i said: Every jewelry prepared for permissible dress: zakat is not obligatory on it. For us: what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, saw two women performing tawaf, and on them were two bracelets of gold, and he said: Do you pay their zakat? They said: No. He said: Would you like that Allah should encircle you with bracelets of fire of Hell? They said: No. He said: Then pay their zakat. As for rubies, pearls, and jewels: there is no zakat on them even if they are jewelry, unless they are for trade.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage addresses zakat on gold and silver that is not in the form of coins. The matn states that zakat is due on tibr (raw gold/silver from the mine, unwrought), jewelry (حلي) made from them, and utensils (آنية) made from them. The commentator defines tibr as the material extracted from the mine, unminted. Then it presents the Shafi'i objection: al-Shafi'i holds that jewelry prepared for permissible (mubah) wear is exempt from zakat. The Hanafi response is based on a hadith in which the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded two women to pay zakat on their gold bracelets, indicating that jewelry is subject to zakat. The commentator then adds that precious stones (rubies, pearls, jewels) are not subject to zakat even if used as jewelry, because they are not gold or silver; unless they are held for trade, in which case they are treated as trade goods. This is an inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on the zakatability of permissible jewelry. The hadith serves as the Hanafi proof, showing that the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly required zakat on gold bracelets, which were clearly jewelry for adornment. The Hanafi position is that gold and silver in any form are zakatable once they reach nisab and hawl, with no exemption for personal use items.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Unfabricated gold or silver as extracted from the mine, not yet minted into coins or made into jewelry.
حلي (huly): Jewelry or ornaments made from gold or silver.
آنية (aniyah): Utensils or vessels made from gold or silver.

Key Takeaway
Gold and silver jewelry is subject to zakat in Hanafi law based on explicit hadith, regardless of use.

Zakat on Gold and Silver Ornaments and Utensils
Commentary on the obligation of zakat on gold/silver ornaments and utensils, with proof against Shafi'i and internal differences on payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat of gold/silver ornaments and utensils, explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on payment method.

Core Idea
Gold and silver ornaments are always subject to zakat in the Hanafi school; payment method depends on paying in kind or value.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayra explains the Hanafi ruling that zakat is wajib on gold and silver ornaments and utensils, regardless of whether they are worn or stored. It presents the Shafi'i objection and refutes it with a hadith. The passage then explores intra-Hanafi differences on how to pay zakat when paying from value, a practical issue for wealthy households.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State that the Hanafi school makes zakat wajib on all forms of gold and silver, including bullion, ornaments, and utensils. Note the conditions of nisab and one-year ownership (implied).
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Locate the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i exempts ornaments prepared for permissible wear, arguing they are like clothing and not mal-e-nami (growing wealth).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The hadith of the two women with gold bracelets: the Prophet commanded them to pay zakat, using an imperative indicating obligation. The threat of punishment reinforces the ruling.
The hadith is ahad, making the ruling wajib not fard.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis pay zakat annually on all gold jewelry; Shafi'is do not unless it is for trade.
5
Differentiate intra-Hanafi views on payment method
When paying zakat from value (e.g., paying dirhams for a silver vessel), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider only weight; Muhammad considers quality; Zufar considers value. The mufta bihi is quantity-based.
For utensils, consensus exists on obligation but not on payment method.

وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا أدى خمسة دراهم: جاز؛ لأن الحكم عنده مقصور على الوزن.
وإن أدى من الذهب ما تبلغ قيمته خمسة دراهم: لم يجز، إجماعاً؛ لأن الجودة متقومة عند المقابلة، بخلاف الجنس.
والأصل في هذا أن المال الذي تجب فيه الزكاة: إن كان مما تجري فيه الربا: فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف يعتبر فيه القدر، دون القيمة.

وعند محمد : أنفع الوجهين للفقراء.
بيانه: إذا كان له مائتا قفيز حنطة للتجارة، قيمتها: مائتا درهم، حال عليها الحول، وقيمتها كذلك فعليه خمسة أقفزة جيدة.
Chapter of Zakat of Gold. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Whatever exceeds twenty, its zakat is according to its calculation. And in gold and silver bullion, their ornaments, and utensils made from them: zakat is due. (And according to them both: zakat is obligatory on the increase over twenty according to its calculation). His saying: (And in) gold and silver bullion, their ornaments, and utensils made from them: zakat. Bullion (al-tibr): the piece extracted from the mine, and it is not minted. And his saying: and their ornaments: al-Shafi'i said: Every ornament prepared for permissible wearing: zakat is not obligatory in it. For us (the Hanafis) is what was narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw two women performing tawaf, and on them were bracelets of gold. He said: 'Do you pay their zakat?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Would you like that Allah should encircle you with bracelets of fire of Hell?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then pay their zakat.' As for rubies, pearls, and jewels, there is no zakat on them even if they are ornaments, unless they are for trade. As for utensils made of gold and silver and the like and others: zakat is obligatory in them, without dispute, but the ruling differs between payment from the same type and payment from its value. For example, if one has a silver vessel weighing two hundred and worth three hundred, then if he pays from its same type: he gives charity with one-fortieth of it to the poor, so they share in it. And if he pays from its value: according to Muhammad, he converts to a different type, i.e., gold, because quality is considered according to him. And according to Abu Hanifa: if he pays five dirhams, it is permissible, because the ruling is restricted to weight. And if he pays from gold an amount whose value is five dirhams: it is not permissible, by consensus, because quality is compensable in exchange, unlike the same type. And the principle in this is that wealth in which zakat is obligatory: if it is of the type in which riba applies: then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, quantity is considered, not value. According to Zufar: value, not quantity. And according to Muhammad: whichever of the two ways is more beneficial for the poor. Its explanation: if he has two hundred qafiz of wheat for trade, its value is two hundred dirhams, the year has passed, and its value is still that, then he owes five good qafiz.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Zakat of Gold from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It begins with the ruling that for gold exceeding twenty mithqal, zakat is due proportionally. Bullion (tibr) refers to unminted gold and silver from mines; zakat is due on it. Ornaments made of gold and silver also incur zakat according to the Hanafi school. The commentator then presents the Shafi'i view that ornaments prepared for permissible wear are exempt, and refutes it with a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded two women with gold bracelets to pay zakat. The hadith is cited as proof that ornaments are subject to zakat. Precious stones like rubies and pearls are exempt unless they are trade goods. The passage then discusses utensils made of gold and silver; there is consensus that zakat is obligatory, but the method of payment differs. If one pays from the same metal (e.g., silver from silver), he gives 1/40 of the weight. If paying from value, the Hanafi scholars differ: Muhammad requires payment in a different metal (gold) to account for quality, while Abu Hanifa allows payment in dirhams because only weight matters. Paying from gold for a silver vessel is invalid by consensus because quality is compensable. The underlying principle for ribawi items: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider quantity, Zufar considers value, and Muhammad chooses the more beneficial for the poor. The example of wheat illustrates this: if two hundred qafiz of wheat are valued at two hundred dirhams, then five good qafiz are due, focusing on quantity.

Key Terms
التبر (al-tibr): Gold or silver extracted from the mine, unminted, in its raw form.
الحلي (al-hulli): Ornaments made from gold or silver, such as bracelets, necklaces, etc.
الآنية (al-āniyah): Utensils and vessels made from gold or silver.
الجودة (al-jūdah): Quality of the metal (e.g., purity, craftsmanship) that affects its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates zakat on all gold/silver ornaments and utensils, and the payment method depends on whether one pays in kind or value, with the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) considering quantity only.

Zakat Payment: Quantity vs Value for Ribawi Items
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat payment method for ribawi goods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether quantity or value is considered when paying zakat on ribawi items, and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
For ribawi items, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider only quantity; Muhammad and Zufar differ, but the school relies on quantity.

This passage delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat payment: when a person owes zakat on a ribawi commodity (like silver or wheat), is the payment valid if the weight/measure matches but the quality differs? The disagreement centers on whether the prohibition of riba requires equality in value or just in quantity. We will walk through the positions of the Hanafi imams and see how they apply to various practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: for ribawi items, only quantity (weight/volume) matters; quality is irrelevant. This is the relied-upon view in the school.
This view is based on the principle that riba is avoided by equality of measure, not value.
2
Identify the opposing views
Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar differ. Muhammad says to choose whichever is more beneficial for the poor. Zufar says only value matters, regardless of quantity.
These are the two minority intra-Hanafi positions.
3
Work through the key scenario
Take the example of a silver vessel weighing 200 dirhams but worth 300. If the owner pays 5 good dirhams (weight), Abu Hanifa says it's valid; if he pays gold worth 5 dirhams, it's invalid by consensus because gold is a different ribawi type.
This shows the practical consequence: paying inferior silver of same weight is fine for Abu Hanifa.
4
Apply to wheat and coin examples
Analyze the wheat examples: if someone owes 5 good qafiz, borrowing 5 inferior qafiz (worth 4) suffices for Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf. For Muhammad/Zufar, extra value must be paid. Similarly for dirhams: good coins paid with bad coins of same weight is valid for the majority.
Note the pattern: for ribawi items, the dispute affects the sufficiency of payment.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
In the Hanafi school, the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (quantity only) is the relied-upon view. This is because it is the zahir al-riwayah and fits best with the principles of zakat facilitation.
For non-ribawi items, value is considered, but here the item is ribawi.

باب زكاة الذهب
- وأما الآنية المتخذة من الذهب والفضة والألجمة، وغيرها: فالزكاة فيها واجبة، بلا خلاف، ولكن يختلف الحكم فيها بين الأداء من عينها، والأداء من قيمتها :
فإنه إذا كان له إناء من فضة وزنه مائتان وقيمته ثلاثمائة، فإن أدى
من عينه : تصدق بربع عشره على الفقير، فيشاركه فيه. - وإن أدى من قيمته: فعند محمد : يعدل إلى خلاف الجنس، وهو الذهب ؛ لأن الجودة عنده معتبرة.
وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا أدى خمسة دراهم: جاز؛ لأن الحكم عنده مقصور على الوزن.
وإن أدى من الذهب ما تبلغ قيمته خمسة دراهم: لم يجز، إجماعاً؛
لأن الجودة متقومة عند المقابلة، بخلاف الجنس.
والأصل في هذا أن المال الذي تجب فيه الزكاة: إن كان مما تجري فيه الربا: فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف يعتبر فيه القدر، دون القيمة.

وعند محمد : أنفع الوجهين للفقراء.
بيانه: إذا كان له مائتا قفيز حنطة للتجارة، قيمتها: مائتا درهم، حال
عليها الحول، وقيمتها كذلك فعليه خمسة أقفزة جيدة.

فإن استقرض خمسة أقفزة رديئة قيمتها أربعة دراهم، فأداها عن هذه: أجزأه، وسقطت عنه الزكاة عندهما، ولا يجب عليه شيء غير ذلك؛ لأن الزيادة رباً.
وقال محمد وزفر عليه أن يؤدي الفضل إلى تمام قيمة الواجب.
:
ولو كان له مائتا قفيز رديئة قيمتها مائتان فأدى أربعة أقفزة جيدة، قيمتها خمسة دراهم، فأداها عن خمسة أقفزة رديئة: لا يجوز إلا عن أربعة منها، وعليه قفيز آخر، في قول أصحابنا الثلاثة.
وقال زفر : لا شيء عليه غير ذلك ؛ لأنه يعتبر القيمة، دون القدر. و محمد يعتبر أنفعهما للفقراء، وهنا اعتبار القدر أنفع.

وقال محمد وزفر: عليه أن يؤدي الفضل.

Chapter of Zakat on Gold. As for utensils made of gold and silver, and saddles, and others: zakat is obligatory on them, without dispute, but the ruling differs between payment from the same type and payment from its value. If he has a silver vessel weighing two hundred [dirhams] and its value is three hundred, then if he pays from the same type: he gives charity of one-tenth of its quarter to the poor, sharing it with him. If he pays from its value: according to Muhammad: he should convert to a different type, which is gold; because quality is considered according to him. According to Abu Hanifa: if he pays five dirhams: it is permissible; because the ruling is confined to weight. And if he pays gold whose value reaches five dirhams: it is not permissible, by consensus; because quality is valued in exchange, unlike the same type. The principle in this is that wealth upon which zakat is obligatory: if it is subject to riba: then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, quantity is considered, not value. According to Zufar: value, not quantity. According to Muhammad: whichever is more beneficial for the poor. Explanation: If he has two hundred qafiz of wheat for trade, its value two hundred dirhams, a year passed while its value is still that, then he owes five good qafiz. If he borrows five inferior qafiz worth four dirhams, and pays them for this: it suffices, and zakat is dropped from him according to them both, and nothing else is obligatory because the increase is riba. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the difference to complete the value of the obligatory amount. Similarly, if he has two hundred inferior qafiz worth two hundred, and he pays four good qafiz worth five dirhams, paying them for five inferior qafiz: it is not valid except for four of them, and he owes another qafiz, according to the statement of our three companions. Zufar said: nothing else is upon him; because he considers value, not quantity. And Muhammad considers whichever is more beneficial for the poor, and here considering quantity is more beneficial. Similarly, if he has two hundred dirhams of low-quality or mixed coins (nubahrja) that are predominantly silver, and he pays four good ones worth five inferior dirhams: it is not valid except for four, and he owes another dirham, according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else is upon him. If the dirhams are good, and he pays five low-quality ones worth four good ones: zakat drops from him according to them both; because quality is not considered according to them. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the difference. Similarly, if he has a mass of good silver weighing two hundred dirhams, and its value due to its quality and craftsmanship is three hundred: then he owes one-tenth of its quarter; if he pays five low-quality ones: it suffices according to them both.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on paying zakat from gold and silver items, focusing on whether one may pay from the same type or from the value. The author begins by noting that zakat is unanimously obligatory on utensils made of gold and silver, but the method of payment differs. If a person has a silver vessel weighing 200 dirhams but worth 300 dirhams due to craftsmanship, and he pays zakat from the same type (silver), he gives one-quarter of one-tenth (i.e., 2.5% of the weight: 5 dirhams weight) to the poor, sharing the actual vessel. If he pays from the value, Imam Muhammad holds that he should use gold (a different ribawi type) to avoid riba, as he considers quality. Abu Hanifa says paying five dirhams of good silver suffices because only weight matters. Paying gold of equivalent value is invalid by consensus. The underlying principle: for ribawi wealth, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider quantity (weight/volume) not value; Zufar considers value only; Muhammad chooses the more beneficial for the poor. The passage then illustrates with wheat examples: if one has 200 qafiz of good wheat worth 200 dirhams, he owes 5 good qafiz. If he borrows 5 inferior qafiz worth 4 dirhams and pays them, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf deem it valid (no riba because quantity matches), while Muhammad and Zufar require payment of the value difference. Similar examples with dirhams and silver masses follow, clarifying that for non-ribawi items (like crafted silver), quality is considered in value, but the ruling differs based on whether the item is ribawi or not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for ribawi items (quantity matters), but for non-ribawi items, value is considered. However, the text presents multiple views without explicit tarjih.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): Usury or unjustified increase in exchange of certain commodities; prohibited in Islam.
قدر (qadr): Quantity or measure (weight/volume) of a commodity; in this context, the weight of silver or volume of wheat.
قيمة (qīmah): Market value or price of a commodity.
جودة (jūdah): Quality or fineness of a metal (silver/gold) or grain; better quality commands higher value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Valid, because only weight matters.
B) Invalid, because quality must be matched.
C) Valid only if the poor person agrees.
D) Invalid, because of riba.

Key Takeaway
For ribawi items, the Hanafi school relies on the view that only quantity (weight/volume) matters when paying zakat from the same type, ignoring quality differences.

Zakat — Almsgiving

The Hanafi Position on Paying Obligations with Different Quality Goods
Intra-Hanafi dispute over value vs. quantity in fulfilling zakat and vows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on whether value or quantity governs the fulfillment of zakat and vows, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, paying zakat or a vow with different quality goods is valid based on value equivalence, but intra-madhhab disputes arise over whether additional payment is needed.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar commentary presents a series of cases where someone fulfills a zakat or vow obligation using goods of different quality than owed. The central question is whether the obligation is measured by quantity (weight/volume) or by value. Hanafi imams differ, and understanding their reasoning is key to applying the school's rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their general positions
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf generally accept value equivalence, Muhammad sometimes requires exact quantity, and Zufar always considers value alone. Also note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf are referred to as 'al-ithnān' or 'al-ṣāḥibān', while the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are 'al-thalātha'.
The passage uses 'عندهما' for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and 'عند الثلاثة' for the three.
2
Understand the core principle: avoiding riba
When paying inferior goods for an obligation of superior goods, any increase in quantity would be riba if exact quantity is required. Hence Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept value equivalence to avoid riba. When paying superior goods, the concern shifts to benefiting the poor, so value may still prevail.
The concept of istihsan (juristic preference) drives these rulings.
3
Analyze the first case: loan of inferior grain for zakat
If someone borrows five qafiz of inferior grain worth four dirhams and pays it for zakat, the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule it sufficient. The increase in value would be riba if additional payment were required. Muhammad and Zufar require paying the difference to match the value of the obligatory.
This case establishes the pattern for when the payer's goods are of lower quality.
4
Examine the second case: paying good grain for inferior grain
If someone has 200 qafiz of inferior grain worth 200 and pays 4 good qafiz worth 5 for 5 inferior qafiz, the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule it valid only for 4, and he owes another qafiz. Zufar says it is fully valid. Muhammad here considers quantity more beneficial for the poor, while Zufar considers value alone.
This shows that Muhammad sometimes aligns with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the three) and sometimes with Zufar.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under the two, paying inferior goods for superior obligations is sufficient; under Muhammad, additional payment is needed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, except where specified otherwise.
Later authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah uphold this tarjih.

:
وأجمعوا على أنه إذا أدى من الذهب أو من غيره مما سوى الفضة: فعليه قيمة الواجب بالغاً ما بلغ، وهي سبعة ونصف. وكذا الحكم في النذر إذا أوجب على نفسه صدقة قفيز حنطة جيدة،

رديء: لا يجوز إلا عن النصف، عند الثلاثة.

ولو أوجب شاتين، فتصدق بشاة سمينة، تبلغ قيمتها قيمة شاتين:
جاز؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الربا.

وكذا إذا كان الواجب بنت مخاض، فأدى بعض بنت لبون: أجزأه.
Chapter on Zakat of Gold/Silver: If he borrowed five inferior qafiz worth four dirhams, and paid them for this [zakat], it suffices him, and the zakat falls from him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and nothing else is obligatory upon him because the increase would be riba. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess to complete the value of what is obligatory. And if he had two hundred inferior qafiz worth two hundred, and he gave four good qafiz worth five dirhams, paying them for five inferior qafiz: it is not valid except for four of them, and he owes another qafiz, according to the statement of our three companions. Zufar said: nothing else is upon him because he considers value, not quantity. And Muhammad considers what is more beneficial for the poor, and here considering quantity is more beneficial. And if he had two hundred dirhams, mixed or blank [coins], with silver predominant, and he paid four good dirhams worth five inferior dirhams: it is not valid except for four, and he owes another dirham according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else upon him. And if the dirhams were good, and he paid five mixed dirhams worth four good: the zakat falls from him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because quality is disregarded according to them. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess. Similarly, if he had a silver ingot good, weighing two hundred dirhams, and its value due to quality and craftsmanship is three hundred: he owes its quarter of tenth (5 dirhams), and if he paid five mixed dirhams, it suffices him according to the two. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess. And they all agreed that if he pays from gold or from other than silver, he owes the value of the obligatory, whatever it may be, which is seven and a half. Similarly, the ruling in a vow: if he obligated upon himself charity of a qafiz of good wheat, and he paid an inferior qafiz, he exits from his vow according to the two. Muhammad and Zufar said: he owes the excess. And if he obligated an inferior qafiz, and he paid half a good qafiz worth the value of an inferior qafiz: it is not valid except for half, according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else upon him. And if he obligated two sheep, and he gave a fat sheep worth the value of two sheep: it is valid because it does not lead to riba. Similarly in zakat: if two medium sheep are obligatory upon him, and he gave a fat sheep worth the value of two medium sheep, it suffices him. Similarly, if the obligatory was a Bint Makhad (one-year-old she-camel), and he gave some of a Bint Labun (two-year-old she-camel), it suffices him.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the issue of fulfilling obligations (zakat and vows) when the quality of what is given differs from what is owed. The core dispute among Hanafi scholars is whether the obligation is measured by quantity (volume/weight) or by value. The positions can be summarized: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf generally consider value equivalence sufficient, while Muhammad and Zufar sometimes require the exact quantity, especially when the quality is higher or lower. However, in some cases, the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree against Zufar, who consistently prioritizes value. The first case involves a loan of inferior grain used to pay zakat; the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) deem it sufficing, as the increase in value would be riba, while Muhammad and Zufar require payment of the difference. In the second case, paying good grain for inferior grain—the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that only the value equivalent portion is valid, while Zufar considers the entire payment valid. Muhammad's reasoning here is that quantity is more beneficial for the poor. Similar rulings apply for dirhams: when paying good dirhams for inferior ones, the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) accept it because quality is disregarded; Muhammad and Zufar require the difference. When paying inferior dirhams for good ones, the three rule that only the value portion is valid; Zufar accepts the whole. For a silver ingot, the two accept payment of inferior dirhams, but Muhammad and Zufar require the difference. There is consensus (Ijma) that when paying from gold or other than silver, one must pay the exact value (7.5 dirhams in this case). Vows follow similar patterns, with Zufar consistently taking the value-based view. The passage concludes with examples where paying a superior quality animal (fat sheep or older camel) satisfies the obligation, as it does not involve riba and is even more beneficial to the recipient. The rulings reflect the Hanafi methodology of istihsan (juristic preference) and consideration of benefit.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyūf): Defective or debased dirhams that are mixed with other metals but still predominantly silver.
نَبَهرجة (nabahrajah): Blank or counterfeit coins without clear stamp, but with predominant silver content.
قلب فضة (qalb fiḍḍah): A silver ingot or lump, valued not only by weight but also by craftsmanship.
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel one year old, due as zakat on a certain number of camels.
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel two years old, higher quality than bint makhad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The zakat is invalid because the quality is lower.
B) The zakat is valid and nothing extra is required.
C) The zakat is valid only for 4 dirhams and he owes 1 more dirham.
D) He must pay an additional good dirham to make up the value.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school primarily values equivalence of value over exact quantity, with Zufar as the consistent value-holder and Muhammad sometimes prioritizing quantity for the poor's benefit.

Applying the Value vs. Quantity Rule: Specific Cases in Zakat and Vows
Detailed rulings on specific cases of zakat and vow payments with different quality goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the positions of the Hanafi imams to determine the validity of zakat and vow payments when goods of different quality are given in specific scenarios involving grain, dirhams, gold, animals, and vows.

Core Idea
Each case (grain, dirhams, animals) has a unique ruling depending on the direction of quality difference and the imam's principle, with the three often agreeing against Zufar on cases where quantity is more beneficial.

In this lesson, we systematically go through each specific case presented in the passage: grain payments, dirham payments (including zuyuf and nabahrajah), silver ingot payments, payments from gold or other metals, and animal payments in zakat and vows. For each case, we note which imams agree and where Zufar diverges. Understanding these details is crucial for accurate fatwa application.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the case by type of goods
Identify whether the case involves grain, dirhams, silver ingot, gold/other metals, or animals. Each has its own rules due to the nature of the goods (riba, valuation, etc.).
Most cases involve ribawi items (grain, silver, gold) where value equivalence is more complex.
2
Identify the direction of quality difference
Determine whether the payer is giving inferior goods for a superior obligation, or superior goods for an inferior obligation. This direction often determines the ruling.
Paying inferior for superior triggers riba concerns; paying superior for inferior may trigger benefit to the poor.
3
Recall the positions of the imams for that scenario
For each scenario, state the ruling according to Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (the two), Muhammad, Zufar, and when the three agree. The passage specifies these explicitly.
Use the passage as a reference: 'عندهما', 'عند الثلاثة', 'وقال محمد/زفر'.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario
Based on the positions, determine whether the payment is valid, and if any additional payment is required. Note the thamarah al-khilaf.
The mufta bihi for most cases follows the two, but exceptions exist.

وقال محمد وزفر عليه أن يؤدي الفضل إلى تمام قيمة الواجب.
:
ولو كان له مائتا قفيز رديئة قيمتها مائتان فأدى أربعة أقفزة جيدة، قيمتها خمسة دراهم، فأداها عن خمسة أقفزة رديئة: لا يجوز إلا عن أربعة منها، وعليه قفيز آخر، في قول أصحابنا الثلاثة.
وقال زفر : لا شيء عليه غير ذلك ؛ لأنه يعتبر القيمة، دون القدر. و محمد يعتبر أنفعهما للفقراء، وهنا اعتبار القدر أنفع.
ولو كان له مائتا درهم ،زيوف أو نَبَهرجة، الغالب عليها الفضة، فأدى عنها أربعة جيدة، تبلغ قيمتها خمسة دراهم رديئة: لا يجوز إلا عن أربعة، وعليه درهم آخر، عند الثلاثة.
وقال زفر : لا شيء عليه غيرها.
ولو كانت الدراهم جيدةً، فأدى عنها خمسة زيوفاً، قيمتها أربعة جيدة : سقطت عنه الزكاة عندهما ؛ لأن الجودة . ساقطة ا العبرة عندهما.
وقال محمد وزفر: عليه أن يؤدي الفضل.
وكذا إذا كان له قلب فضة جيدة، وزنه مائتا درهم، وقيمته لجودته وصناعته ثلاثمائة : فعليه ربع عشره، فإن أدى خمسة زيوفاً: أجزأه عندهما.
وقال محمد وزفر عليه أن يؤدي الفضل.
:
وأجمعوا على أنه إذا أدى من الذهب أو من غيره مما سوى الفضة: فعليه قيمة الواجب بالغاً ما بلغ، وهي سبعة ونصف. وكذا الحكم في النذر إذا أوجب على نفسه صدقة قفيز حنطة جيدة،
فأدى قفيزاً رديئاً: خرج عن نذره عندهما.
وقال محمد وزفر عليه الفضل.
فلو أوجب قفيزاً رديئاً، فأدى نصف قفيز جيد تبلغ قيمته قيمة قفيز
رديء: لا يجوز إلا عن النصف، عند الثلاثة.
وقال زفر: لا شيء عليه غيره.
ولو أوجب شاتين، فتصدق بشاة سمينة، تبلغ قيمتها قيمة شاتين:
جاز؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الربا.
-
وكذا في الزكاة إذا وجب عليه شاتان وسطاً، فأدى شاة سمينة تبلغ
قيمتها قيمة شاتين وسطين: أجزأه.
وكذا إذا كان الواجب بنت مخاض، فأدى بعض بنت لبون: أجزأه.
Chapter on Zakat of Gold/Silver: If he borrowed five inferior qafiz worth four dirhams, and paid them for this [zakat], it suffices him, and the zakat falls from him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and nothing else is obligatory upon him because the increase would be riba. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess to complete the value of what is obligatory. And if he had two hundred inferior qafiz worth two hundred, and he gave four good qafiz worth five dirhams, paying them for five inferior qafiz: it is not valid except for four of them, and he owes another qafiz, according to the statement of our three companions. Zufar said: nothing else is upon him because he considers value, not quantity. And Muhammad considers what is more beneficial for the poor, and here considering quantity is more beneficial. And if he had two hundred dirhams, mixed or blank [coins], with silver predominant, and he paid four good dirhams worth five inferior dirhams: it is not valid except for four, and he owes another dirham according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else upon him. And if the dirhams were good, and he paid five mixed dirhams worth four good: the zakat falls from him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because quality is disregarded according to them. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess. Similarly, if he had a silver ingot good, weighing two hundred dirhams, and its value due to quality and craftsmanship is three hundred: he owes its quarter of tenth (5 dirhams), and if he paid five mixed dirhams, it suffices him according to the two. Muhammad and Zufar said: he must pay the excess. And they all agreed that if he pays from gold or from other than silver, he owes the value of the obligatory, whatever it may be, which is seven and a half. Similarly, the ruling in a vow: if he obligated upon himself charity of a qafiz of good wheat, and he paid an inferior qafiz, he exits from his vow according to the two. Muhammad and Zufar said: he owes the excess. And if he obligated an inferior qafiz, and he paid half a good qafiz worth the value of an inferior qafiz: it is not valid except for half, according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else upon him. And if he obligated two sheep, and he gave a fat sheep worth the value of two sheep: it is valid because it does not lead to riba. Similarly in zakat: if two medium sheep are obligatory upon him, and he gave a fat sheep worth the value of two medium sheep, it suffices him. Similarly, if the obligatory was a Bint Makhad (one-year-old she-camel), and he gave some of a Bint Labun (two-year-old she-camel), it suffices him.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the issue of fulfilling obligations (zakat and vows) when the quality of what is given differs from what is owed. The core dispute among Hanafi scholars is whether the obligation is measured by quantity (volume/weight) or by value. The positions can be summarized: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf generally consider value equivalence sufficient, while Muhammad and Zufar sometimes require the exact quantity, especially when the quality is higher or lower. However, in some cases, the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree against Zufar, who consistently prioritizes value. The first case involves a loan of inferior grain used to pay zakat; the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) deem it sufficing, as the increase in value would be riba, while Muhammad and Zufar require payment of the difference. In the second case, paying good grain for inferior grain—the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that only the value equivalent portion is valid, while Zufar considers the entire payment valid. Muhammad's reasoning here is that quantity is more beneficial for the poor. Similar rulings apply for dirhams: when paying good dirhams for inferior ones, the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) accept it because quality is disregarded; Muhammad and Zufar require the difference. When paying inferior dirhams for good ones, the three rule that only the value portion is valid; Zufar accepts the whole. For a silver ingot, the two accept payment of inferior dirhams, but Muhammad and Zufar require the difference. There is consensus (Ijma) that when paying from gold or other than silver, one must pay the exact value (7.5 dirhams in this case). Vows follow similar patterns, with Zufar consistently taking the value-based view. The passage concludes with examples where paying a superior quality animal (fat sheep or older camel) satisfies the obligation, as it does not involve riba and is even more beneficial to the recipient. The rulings reflect the Hanafi methodology of istihsan (juristic preference) and consideration of benefit.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyūf): Defective or debased dirhams that are mixed with other metals but still predominantly silver.
نَبَهرجة (nabahrajah): Blank or counterfeit coins without clear stamp, but with predominant silver content.
قلب فضة (qalb fiḍḍah): A silver ingot or lump, valued not only by weight but also by craftsmanship.
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel one year old, due as zakat on a certain number of camels.
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel two years old, higher quality than bint makhad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), what is the ruling when someone pays 4 good dirhams (worth 5 inferior dirhams) for a zakat of 5 inferior dirhams?
A) The zakat is fully paid.
B) The zakat is paid for 4 dirhams only; he owes 1 more inferior dirham.
C) The payment is invalid.
D) He must pay an additional good dirham.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the validity of paying different quality goods for zakat or vows depends on the specific case, with the three often requiring quantity equivalence when superior goods are given, while Zufar consistently values value.

Substitution in Zakat and Vows: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution in discharging obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreements when discharging zakat or a vow with a different quality or quantity, and apply the rule that substituting a superior item is permissible while an inferior item may require compensation.

Core Idea
Discharging an obligation with a superior item suffices; with an inferior item may require paying the difference – and the Hanafi imams differ on the details.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explores a subtle area of fiqh: when you owe zakat or a vowed item, can you give something of a different quality? The Hanafi school generally permits substitution, but the imams disagree about when compensation (al-fadl) is required. Understanding these rulings helps you grasp the structure of obligation and discharge in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and the substitution
State clearly what is owed (e.g., a good qafiz of wheat, two medium sheep, a Bint Makhad) and what is given instead (e.g., a bad qafiz, one fat sheep, a Bint Labun). This frames the legal problem.
2
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify which Hanafi imam takes which position. The text records disagreements between the 'three' (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Zufar, and also between 'the two' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) versus Muhammad and Zufar.
Pay attention to who is included in 'the three' and 'the two' in each scenario.
3
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For each factual scenario (e.g., good wheat for bad, bad wheat for half good, two sheep for one fat sheep, Bint Makhad for Bint Labun), state whether the obligation is fully discharged, partially discharged, or requires additional payment.
4
Find the common principle
Notice a consistent theme: substituting a superior item is always accepted (fat sheep for two medium, Bint Labun for Bint Makhad). The disagreement centres on substituting an inferior item.
Analogy: paying extra does not lead to riba, so it's permissible.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Ask: what practical difference does the disagreement make? For example, if someone vowed a bad qafiz and gave half a good one, Zufar considers the vow fulfilled; the three say only half is fulfilled, so the person must still give the other half or its value.

Source Text

وقال محمد وزفر عليه أن يؤدي الفضل.
وأجمعوا على أنه إذا أدى من الذهب أو من غيره مما سوى الفضة: فعليه قيمة الواجب بالغاً ما بلغ، وهي سبعة ونصف. وكذا الحكم في النذر إذا أوجب على نفسه صدقة قفيز حنطة جيدة،
فأدى قفيزاً رديئاً: خرج عن نذره عندهما.
وقال محمد وزفر عليه الفضل.
فلو أوجب قفيزاً رديئاً، فأدى نصف قفيز جيد تبلغ قيمته قيمة قفيز
رديء: لا يجوز إلا عن النصف، عند الثلاثة.
وقال زفر: لا شيء عليه غيره.
ولو أوجب شاتين، فتصدق بشاة سمينة، تبلغ قيمتها قيمة شاتين:
جاز؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الربا.
-
وكذا في الزكاة إذا وجب عليه شاتان وسطاً، فأدى شاة سمينة تبلغ
قيمتها قيمة شاتين وسطين: أجزأه.
وكذا إذا كان الواجب بنت مخاض، فأدى بعض بنت لبون: أجزأه.
Chapter of Zakat of Gold. Muhammad and Zufar said: He must pay the excess. And they are unanimous that if he pays from gold or from other than silver, he must pay the value of the wajib, whatever it may be, which is seven and a half. Likewise the ruling in a vow if he obligates upon himself a charity of a qafiz of good wheat, then he pays a qafiz of bad wheat: he is released from his vow according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad and Zufar said: upon him is the excess. If he obligates a qafiz of bad wheat, then he pays half a qafiz of good wheat whose value reaches the value of a bad qafiz: it is not permissible except for half, according to the three. Zufar said: nothing else is due upon him. If he obligates two sheep, then he gives in charity one fat sheep whose value reaches the value of two sheep: it is permissible because it does not lead to riba. Likewise in zakat, if two medium sheep are due upon him, then he gives one fat sheep whose value reaches the value of two medium sheep: it suffices him. Likewise if a Bint Makhad is due, then he gives a Bint Labun: it suffices him.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a person substitutes a different type or quality of asset when discharging an obligation such as zakat or a vow. The text begins with a statement from Muhammad and Zufar that if one pays from a different type (e.g., gold instead of silver), one must pay the value of the wajib, which is 7.5 dirhams in the case of zakat on silver. Then it moves to vows: if one vows to give a good qafiz but gives a bad one, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the vow is fulfilled, but Muhammad and Zufar say the excess (difference in value) must be paid. Similarly, if one vows a bad qafiz and gives half a good qafiz equal in value, the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say it only counts for half, while Zufar says nothing else is due. The passage then addresses giving a single fat sheep in place of two ordinary sheep, which is allowed because it does not involve riba (usury). The same principle applies in zakat: if two medium sheep are due, one fat sheep worth two suffices; if a Bint Makhad is due, a Bint Labun suffices. The rulings illustrate that substituting a superior item is generally acceptable, but substituting an inferior item may require compensation for the deficiency. The differences among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) show varying approaches to discharge of obligations.

Key Terms
الفضل (al-fadl): The excess value or quantity that must be paid when discharging an obligation with a lesser value than required.
قيمة الواجب (qimat al-wajib): The monetary value of the obligated item; when paying from a different type, one must pay this value.
نذر (nadhr): A vow whereby a person obligates upon himself an act of charity or worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person vows to give a good qafiz of wheat but gives a bad qafiz, what is the ruling according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) The vow is not fulfilled; he must repeat it.
B) The vow is fulfilled and nothing else is due.
C) He must pay the excess (the difference in value).
D) He must give a good qafiz in addition.

Key Takeaway
Substituting an inferior item for an obligation may require compensation for the deficiency, while giving a superior item is acceptable; the Hanafi imams differ on exact applications.
