Zakat on Trade Goods: Valuation and Condition for Obligation
Explaining obligation of zakat on trade goods and the method of valuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for trade goods and distinguish the two valuation methods of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods is due when value reaches nisab; valuation method determines whether zakat is triggered.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah explains the obligation of zakat on trade goods. The author, al-Quduri, sets the condition that the goods' value must reach the nisab of gold or silver. The commentary then delves into the different interpretations among the Hanafi imams regarding which currency to use for valuation, a key practical nuance that can affect whether zakat is payable at all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the ruling from the matn: zakat is obligatory on trade goods when their value reaches the nisab. Note that the condition is the value reaching nisab, not the goods themselves being nisab.
2
Define trade goods (urud al-tijarah)
Understand that trade goods are anything other than gold and silver (the two currencies) that are bought and sold for profit. This excludes personal items and real estate not intended for trade.
3
Analyze the valuation directive
The matn says to value goods by what is most beneficial (al-anfa‘) for the poor. The commentary explains how this is interpreted differently by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Compare the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: value by whichever currency (gold or silver) reaches the nisab (i.e., the lower nisab, typically silver). Abu Yusuf: value by the currency used for purchase; if no cash was used, use the prevalent market currency.
5
Derive the practical consequence
Apply the difference: if goods were bought with gold, Abu Hanifa values by silver (if it reaches nisab, zakat is due); Abu Yusuf values by gold (if gold value is below nisab, no zakat). Identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة العروض

أخره عن النقدين؛ لأنه يقوم بهما.
والعروض: ما سوى النقدين.
قال رحمه الله: (الزكاة واجبة في عروض التجارة، كائنة ما كانت إذا بلغت قيمتها نصاباً من الورق أو الذهب).
قوله: (يقومها بما هو أنفع للفقراء والمساكين منهما).

تفسير الأنفع : أن يقومها بما يبلغ نصاباً عند أبي حنيفة.
وعند أبي يوسف: بما اشتراه إن كان الثمن من النقود، وإن اشتراه بغير النقود : قومها بالنقد الغالب.
Chapter of Zakat of Trade Goods. He delayed it after the two currencies because they are used to value them. And trade goods: what is other than the two currencies. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Zakat is obligatory on trade goods, whatever they may be, if their value reaches a nisab of silver or gold). His statement: (He values them by that which is most beneficial for the poor and needy from the two). Explanation of 'the most beneficial': that he values them by that which reaches a nisab according to Abu Hanifa. And according to Abu Yusuf: by what he bought them with if the price was from currency; if he bought them with non-currency, he values them by the prevalent currency.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on zakat of trade goods. The commentator explains why this chapter is placed after the chapters on gold and silver: because trade goods are valued by these currencies. The definition of 'trade goods' ('urud) is given: anything other than the two currencies (gold and silver coins). The matn from al-Quduri states that zakat is obligatory on trade goods when their value reaches the nisab (minimum threshold) of either silver or gold. The matn also states that the goods are valued by whichever of the two (gold or silver) is most beneficial for the poor and needy. The commentator then explains the differences among the Hanafi imams regarding the interpretation of 'most beneficial'. Abu Hanifa holds that the most beneficial is the one by which the value reaches the nisab (i.e., the lower nisab, since gold's nisab is 20 mithqal and silver's is 200 dirhams; typically the nisab of silver is lower in value, so valuing by silver is more beneficial because it triggers zakat sooner). Abu Yusuf holds that the valuation should be based on the currency used to purchase the goods; if bought with cash, use that cash; if bought by barter, use the prevalent currency in the market. This difference affects the calculation of zakat: for example, if someone bought goods with gold, Abu Hanifa would value them by silver if that reaches nisab, while Abu Yusuf would value by gold.

Key Terms
عروض التجارة (urud al-tijarah): Trade goods: any property (except gold and silver) that is bought and sold for profit.
الأنفع (al-anfa'): Most beneficial; used in valuation context to mean the method that results in the greatest benefit for the poor and needy.
النقد الغالب (al-naqd al-ghalib): The prevalent currency in the market; used by Abu Yusuf when goods are purchased without cash.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does Abu Hanifa interpret 'most beneficial' (الأنفع) when valuing trade goods for zakat?
A) He values by the currency in which the goods were purchased.
B) He values by the prevalent currency in the market.
C) He values by the currency whose value reaches the nisab (i.e., the lower nisab).
D) He values by gold regardless.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods is due when value reaches nisab; the valuation method (Abu Hanifa's silver-based or Abu Yusuf's transaction-based) determines obligation.

Valuation Currency for Zakat on Trade Goods
Explains obligation and dispute on valuation currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on valuing trade goods for zakat when both gold and silver reach nisab, and apply the most beneficial principle.

Core Idea
When both currencies reach nisab, valuation method directly affects zakat due; the most beneficial to the poor is chosen.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the obligation of zakat on trade goods and the intra-Hanafi disagreement on valuation currency. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for accurate zakat calculation, as the choice of currency significantly impacts the amount payable.

Guided Path
1
State the foundational ruling
Identify the act (zakat on trade goods) and its hukm (wajib). Then note that valuation is based on whichever currency is more beneficial for the poor.
The ruling is derived from qiyas on gold and silver.
2
Define the disagreement scenario
The ikhtilaf arises only when the trade goods reach nisab in both gold and silver simultaneously. If only one reaches, there is consensus.
3
Map the three positions
Abu Hanifa: value by the currency that reaches nisab. Abu Yusuf: value by the purchase currency if bought with cash, otherwise by dominant market currency. Muhammad: value by the dominant currency in all cases.
Each scholar's approach leads to a different valuation.
4
Work through the example
Goods worth 240 dirhams or 23 dinars: Abu Hanifa uses dirhams (6 dirhams zakat) rather than dinars (0.5 dinar = 5 dirhams). The text also considers a counter-example where dinars yield more.
The example demonstrates the practical outcome of each position.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is the amount of zakat due. The principle of maslaha (benefit to the poor) governs the choice, favoring the higher payment.
This principle applies across all three positions.

باب زكاة العروض
الزكاة واجبة في عروض التجارة، كائنة ما كانت، إذا بلغت قيمتها نصاباً من الورق أو الذهب.
يقومُها بما هو أنفع للفقراء والمساكين منهما.
باب زكاة العروض
أخره عن النقدين؛ لأنه يقوم بهما.
والعروض: ما سوى النقدين.
قال رحمه الله: (الزكاة واجبةٌ في عروض التجارة، كائنة ما كانت إذا بلغت قيمتها نصاباً من الورق أو الذهب).
أي سواء كانت من جنس ما تجب فيه الزكاة، كالسوائم، أو من غيره، كالثياب والحمير.
* قوله : (يُقومها بما هو أنفع للفقراء والمساكين منهما).
تفسير الأنفع : أن يقومها بما يبلغ نصاباً عند أبي حنيفة.
وعند أبي يوسف: بما اشتراه إن كان الثمن من النقود، وإن اشتراه بغير النقود : قومها بالنقد الغالب.
وعند محمد بالنقد الغالب على كل حال سواء اشتراها بأحد النقدين، أو بغيره.
والخلاف فيما إذا كانت تبلغ بكلا النقدين نصاباً، أما إذا بلغت بأحدهما: قومها بالبالغ، إجماعاً.
بيانه: أنه إذا قومها بالدراهم : تبلغ مائتين وأربعين درهماً، وإن قومها بالدنانير : تبلغ ثلاثة وعشرين ديناراً:
فإنه يقومها بالدراهم عند أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه يجب عليه ستة دراهم، ولو قومها بالدنانير : يجب نصف مثقال، وهو لا يساوي ستة دراهم؛ لأن قيمة المثقال عندهم: عشرة دراهم.
فإن كان لو قومها بالدنانير : تبلغ أربعة وعشرين، ولو قومها بالدراهم: تبلغ مائتين وستة وثلاثين فإنه يقومها بالدنانير؛ لأنه أنفع للفقراء.
Chapter of Zakat on Trade Goods. Zakat is obligatory on trade goods, whatever they may be, when their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. He values them with whichever is more beneficial for the poor and needy between the two. Chapter of Zakat on Trade Goods. He delayed it after the two currencies because it is valued by them. Trade goods: whatever is other than the two currencies. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Zakat is obligatory on trade goods, whatever they may be, when their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold). Meaning, whether they are of a type in which zakat is obligatory, like grazing livestock, or other than that, like clothes and donkeys. His statement: (He values them with whichever is most beneficial for the poor and needy between the two). Interpretation of 'most beneficial': that he values them by whatever reaches the nisab according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf: by what he purchased them with if the price was in currency, and if he purchased them with other than currency: he values them by the dominant currency. According to Muhammad: by the dominant currency in all cases, whether he purchased them with one of the two currencies or with other than them. The disagreement is when both currencies reach the nisab. As for when it reaches nisab by one of them: he values it by the one that reaches, by consensus. Explanation: if he values them by dirhams: they amount to 240 dirhams, and if he values them by dinars: they amount to 23 dinars: then he values them by dirhams according to Abu Hanifa, because six dirhams become obligatory upon him, and if he valued them by dinars, half a mithqal would become obligatory, which does not equal six dirhams, because the value of a mithqal according to them is ten dirhams. And if, when he valued them by dinars, they amount to twenty-four, and when valued by dirhams, they amount to two hundred and thirty-six, then he values them by dinars, because it is more beneficial for the poor.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar discusses the obligation of zakat on trade goods and the method of valuation. The author first states the ruling: zakat is obligatory on all trade goods when their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The valuation must be done using whichever of the two currencies (silver dirhams or gold dinars) is more beneficial to the poor. The commentator then explains the intra-Hanafi disagreement on how to determine 'most beneficial'. Abu Hanifa considers the currency that reaches the nisab threshold as the basis, but this also aligns with being more beneficial because it yields a larger zakat amount. The example given: if goods are worth 240 dirhams or 23 dinars, both reach nisab (200 dirhams and 20 dinars respectively). Abu Hanifa uses dirhams because it results in 6 dirhams zakat (1/40 of 240), whereas using dinars yields 0.5 dinar (1/40 of 20 dinars? Actually 23 dinars is above 20, so 1/40 of 23? No, the text says using dinars would yield half a mithqal, which is 0.5 dinar, worth 5 dirhams. So dirhams give more. Abu Yusuf considers the original purchase currency if the goods were bought with cash, otherwise uses the dominant market currency. Muhammad always uses the dominant currency. The disagreement only arises when both currencies reach nisab; if only one does, there is consensus to use that one. The overall principle is maslaha (benefit to the poor).

Key Terms
العروض (al-‘urūḍ): Trade goods, i.e., all commodities other than gold and silver currency.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation. For silver: 200 dirhams; for gold: 20 dinars.
أنفع (anfa‘): More beneficial. In this context, the valuation method that yields a greater benefit to the poor, either by reaching nisab or by yielding a larger zakat amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the intra-Hanafi disagreement on valuation currency arise?
A) Always when the trader has trade goods
B) Only when both gold and silver reach nisab
C) Only when only one currency reaches nisab
D) Only when the trader purchased goods with credit

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes benefit to the poor (anfa') when valuing trade goods for zakat, and internal ikhtilaf on method is resolved by choosing the most beneficial outcome.

Valuation Time for Zakat on Trade Goods: End of Haul vs. Payment Day
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation timing for zakat on trade goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples regarding the valuation date for zakat on trade goods and identify the practical consequence when payment is made in kind.

Core Idea
Both Abu Hanifa and the disciples agree on the quantity when paying in kind; the dispute only affects payment in cash or value.

Zakat on trade goods requires valuing the stock to calculate the due amount. But when should that valuation occur? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa fixes the valuation at the end of the haul year, while his two disciples prefer the day of actual payment. We'll analyze the reasoning and see that in one specific scenario, both views converge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State Abu Hanifa's position (valuation at end of haul) and the two disciples' position (valuation at payment day).
2
Understand the example
Work through the example: 200 qafiz of wheat worth 200 at haul end, dropping to 100 at payment. Determine zakat under each view if paying in kind.
Paying in kind means giving actual wheat.
3
Analyze the consensus
Note that when paying in kind, both views yield the same quantity (5 qafiz). This is agreed upon by consensus (ijma').
The quantity is fixed at 1/40 of the original amount regardless of value change.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: the dispute only manifests when paying in cash or other goods, not when paying in kind.
If value decreases, Abu Hanifa requires the original amount (e.g., 5 dirhams), while the two would require less (e.g., 2.5 dirhams).
5
Implication for fatwa
Consider which view is mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa's view is generally relied upon for consistency and ease.
Later Hanafi scholars have discussed this ikhtilaf; the text does not resolve it.

Source Text

ثم المعتبر في القيمة عند أبي حنيفة : يومَ الحول، ولا يلتفت بعد ذلك إلى زيادة القيمة ونقصانها.
وعندهما: يوم الأداء إلى الفقراء.
كما إذا كان معه مائتا قفيز حنطة حال عليها الحول، وهي تساوي مائتين، فلم يؤد زكاتها حتى نقصت قيمتها، فصارت تساوي مائة: فإن أدى من الطعام أدى ربع عشره: خمسة أقفزة، إجماعاً.
Then the consideration of value according to Abu Hanifa is the day of the year (end of haul), and after that no attention is paid to increase or decrease in value. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the day of payment to the poor. For example: if someone has two hundred qafiz of wheat, one year passes over them, and they are worth two hundred, then he does not pay its zakat until its value decreases, so it becomes worth one hundred: if he pays from the food (wheat), he pays one-tenth of a quarter of it: five qafiz, by consensus.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses the timing of valuation for zakat on trade goods. Abu Hanifa considers the end of the haul (lunar year) as the reference point for assessing value; subsequent changes in market price are ignored. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the day of actual payment to the poor as the valuation date. The example illustrates the practical effect: if someone has 200 qafiz of wheat worth 200 dirhams at the end of the haul, but the price drops to 100 dirhams before he pays, and he chooses to pay in kind (wheat), he must still give 5 qafiz (1/40 of 200) regardless of the price drop. This is agreed upon (ijma). The disagreement would only affect cases where he pays in value from other goods, but the example shows that paying in kind avoids the dispute. The text clarifies that the two disciples' view would consider the lower value at payment time, but since payment is in kind, the quantity is fixed.

Key Terms
الحول (al-ḥawl): The lunar year that must pass on the wealth for zakat to become due. For trade goods, it is the completion of one year of ownership.
يوم الأداء (yawm al-adā’): The day when the zakat is actually given to the poor. The valuation is done then according to the two disciples.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Valuing Trade Goods for Zakat: Currency and Timing
Explaining intra-Hanafi disputes on currency and date for valuing trade goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on currency and date for valuing trade goods for zakat and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Value trade goods at haul with the currency best for the poor; Sahibayn value at payment.

This passage delves into two key disputes within the Hanafi school on the valuation of trade goods for zakat: which currency to use when goods meet nisab in both gold and silver, and at what point in time the valuation is fixed. The positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani are contrasted, with practical examples illustrating the differences in zakat liability when prices fluctuate or goods undergo intrinsic changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed issues
The passage addresses two separate questions: (1) which currency (gold dinar or silver dirham) to value trade goods when they reach nisab in both, and (2) on what date is the valuation made – the end of the haul (lunar year) or the day the zakat is paid.
Both disputes are within the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa vs. the two students).
2
Analyze the currency dispute
Examine how Muhammad al-Shaybani's view (always use the prevalent currency) differs from Abu Hanifa's (choose the valuation that yields more benefit for the poor). Understand the reasoning: Abu Hanifa prefers the valuation that results in a higher zakat payment to benefit the poor.
The text provides numerical examples: e.g., if goods are worth 240 dirhams or 23 dinars, Abu Hanifa uses dirhams because 6 dirhams > 0.5 mithqal (worth 5 dirhams).
3
Analyze the timing dispute
Study the different valuation dates: Abu Hanifa uses the day the haul is completed (end of the zakat year), while the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use the day of actual payment to the poor. Consider the textual examples with wheat that increases or decreases in price after the haul.
For example, if wheat worth 200 at haul drops to 100 at payment, Abu Hanifa requires 5 dirhams (based on original value), but Sahibayn require 2.5 dirhams.
4
Distinguish price changes from intrinsic changes
The passage notes that the timing dispute applies to price fluctuations (market value). For intrinsic changes (e.g., moisture, weevil damage, drying), the valuation at haul is disregarded and consensus rulings apply based on actual value at payment.
This is an important exception that shows the boundary of the disagreement.
5
Apply the ruling on haul intervals
Understand the rule: if the nisab is complete at both the beginning and end of the haul, a temporary decrease in between does not invalidate the zakat obligation. The text justifies this by the difficulty of maintaining nisab throughout the entire year.
This is a standard Hanafi principle that provides flexibility.

باب زكاة العروض وعند محمد بالنقد الغالب على كل حال سواء اشتراها بأحد النقدين، أو بغيره. والخلاف فيما إذا كانت تبلغ بكلا النقدين نصاباً، أما إذا بلغت بأحدهما: قومها بالبالغ، إجماعاً. بيانه: أنه إذا قومها بالدراهم : تبلغ مائتين وأربعين درهماً، وإن قومها بالدنانير : تبلغ ثلاثة وعشرين ديناراً: فإنه يقومها بالدراهم عند أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه يجب عليه ستة دراهم، ولو قومها بالدنانير : يجب نصف مثقال، وهو لا يساوي ستة دراهم؛ لأن قيمة المثقال عندهم: عشرة دراهم. فإن كان لو قومها بالدنانير : تبلغ أربعة وعشرين، ولو قومها بالدراهم: تبلغ مائتين وستة وثلاثين فإنه يقومها بالدنانير؛ لأنه أنفع للفقراء. ثم المعتبر في القيمة عند أبي حنيفة : يومَ الحول، ولا يلتفت بعد ذلك إلى زيادة القيمة ونقصانها. وعندهما: يوم الأداء إلى الفقراء. كما إذا كان معه مائتا قفيز حنطة حال عليها الحول، وهي تساوي مائتين، فلم يؤد زكاتها حتى نقصت قيمتها، فصارت تساوي مائة: فإن أدى من الطعام أدى ربع عشره: خمسة أقفزة، إجماعاً. وإذا كان النصاب كاملاً في طرفي الحول : فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك لا يُسقط الزكاة. وإن أدى من القيمة : أدى خمسة دراهم عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: درهمين ونصفاً. - وإن كان هذا الطعام زاد بعد الحول في السعر، حتى صار يساوي أربعمائة : فإن أدى من عينه: أدى ربع عشره، إجماعاً. وإن أدى من القيمة : أدى خمسة دراهم عنده، وعندهما: عشرة دراهم. - وهذا إذا كانت الزيادة والنقصان من حيث السعر، أما إذا كانت من حيث الذات، بواسطة الجفاف، أو البَلَل ، أو أكل السوس بعضه، فنقص، كما إذا ابتلت الحنطة بعد الحول، حتى صارت قيمتها مائة، وقد كانت قيمتها يوم الحول مائتين أو أكل السوس بعضها، حتى صارت تساوي مائة: فإن أدى من عينها فخمسة أقفزة، وإن أدى من قيمتها: فدرهمان ونصف، إجماعاً. وإن كان التغيير إلى زيادة بأن كانت يوم الحول مبتلة، وقيمتها مائتان فیبست حتى صارت تساوي أربعمائة : فإن أدى من العين : فخمسة أقفزة، وإن أدى من القيمة فخمسة دراهم، إجماعاً؛ لأن المستفاد بعد الحول: لا يُضم، ونقصان النصاب: يسقط قدره من الزكاة. * قوله: (وإذا كان النصاب كاملاً في طرفي الحول: فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك لا يُسقط الزكاة) ؛ لأنه يَشقُ اعتبار الكمال في أثنائه.
Chapter on zakat of trade goods. And according to Muhammad, [it is valued] by the prevalent currency in all cases, whether he bought them with one of the two currencies or with something else. The dispute is when [the goods] reach nisab with both currencies; as for when they reach nisab with one of them, they are valued by that [currency] by consensus. Its explanation: if he values them by dirhams, they amount to two hundred and forty dirhams; if he values them by dinars, they amount to twenty-three dinars. Then he values them by dirhams according to Abu Hanifa, because he must pay six dirhams; if he valued them by dinars, he would pay half a mithqal, which is not equal to six dirhams, because the value of a mithqal according to them is ten dirhams. If, had he valued them by dinars, they would amount to twenty-four, and had he valued them by dirhams, they would amount to two hundred and thirty-six, then he values them by dinars because it is more beneficial for the poor. Then, the consideration of value according to Abu Hanifa is the day of the haul; he does not pay attention thereafter to increase or decrease in value. And according to the two [students], it is the day of payment to the poor. For example, if he has two hundred qafiz of wheat, a haul has passed over it, and it is worth two hundred, then he did not pay its zakat until its value decreased to one hundred: if he pays from the food, he pays one-tenth of its quarter: five qafiz, by consensus. If the nisab is complete at both ends of the haul, its decrease in between does not cancel the zakat. And if he pays from the value, he pays five dirhams according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, two and a half dirhams. And if this food increased after the haul in price until it became worth four hundred: if he pays from its essence, he pays one-tenth of its quarter, by consensus. And if he pays from the value, he pays five dirhams according to him, and according to the two, ten dirhams. This is if the increase and decrease are in terms of price. As for if they are in terms of essence, by means of drying, moisture, or some of it being eaten by weevils, then it decreases, as if the wheat became moist after the haul until its value became one hundred, whereas its value on the haul day was two hundred, or weevils ate some of it until it became worth one hundred: if he pays from its essence, then five qafiz; if he pays from its value, then two and a half dirhams, by consensus. And if the change is to an increase, such that on the haul day it was moist and its value was two hundred, then it dried until it became worth four hundred: if he pays from the essence, then five qafiz; if he pays from the value, then five dirhams, by consensus; because what is gained after the haul is not added, and a decrease in the nisab cancels its portion of zakat. His statement: 'If the nisab is complete at both ends of the haul, its decrease in between does not cancel the zakat' because it is difficult to consider completeness in its intervals.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valuation of trade goods for zakat. It first addresses which currency to use when goods reach nisab in both gold and silver, with Abu Hanifa preferring the valuation that yields more benefit for the poor, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) always uses the prevalent currency. Then it discusses the timing of valuation: Abu Hanifa holds that the value at the end of the haul (one lunar year) is the basis, and subsequent price changes are ignored, while the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the value at the time of payment. The text provides examples with wheat, illustrating the effect of price fluctuations and intrinsic changes like moisture or weevil damage. It concludes with a note that if the nisab is met at the beginning and end of the haul, temporary decreases in between do not negate zakat.

Key Terms
النقد الغالب (al-naqd al-ghalib): The prevalent currency (gold or silver) in the land at the time of valuation.
القيمة (al-qīmah): The monetary value of trade goods at a specific date (haul or payment).
الحول (al-ḥawl): The lunar year after which zakat becomes due on trade goods.

Nisab Complete at Both Ends: Deficiency in Between Does Not Cancel Zakat
Ruling on zakat obligation when nisab fluctuates during the year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that if nisab is complete at both ends of the zakat year, fluctuations in between do not affect the obligation, and you will be able to distinguish between intra-Hanafi positions on paying zakat from increased value.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods depends only on nisab at start and end of the year, not on mid-year fluctuations.

The Hanafi school recognises the practical challenges traders face: goods constantly change in value, animals are born or die. This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses one of the most common questions: if the nisab drops below the threshold mid-year, does zakat remain due? The answer is yes, provided the nisab was complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year. The passage then explores scenarios of price and quality changes, and introduces an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the sentence: إذا كان النصاب كاملاً في طَرَفَي الحول : فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك لا يُسقط الزكاة. This is the foundational rule: nisab must be complete at the two ends of the year; deficiency in between does not cancel zakat.
The rule applies to trade goods and grazing animals.
2
Analyse the price-change scenario
The text gives an example: food worth two hundred dirhams at the end of the year now worth four hundred. If paying from the same goods, zakat is 1/10 (twenty qafiz? Actually one-tenth of the value, but text says 'ربع عشره'? Wait: ربع عشره means one-fourth of a tenth, which is 1/40? Let's check: Actually the translation says 'one-tenth of it unanimously' but that seems off. In the Arabic it says: ربع عشره which is 1/40? For grain, zakat is 1/10 if irrigated naturally, 1/20 if irrigated artificially. But here it's a general example. We'll follow the text as given. The key is the dispute on paying from value: Abu Hanifa says 5 dirhams (1/40 of 200), Sahibayn say 10 dirhams (1/40 of 400).
The dispute applies only when the increase is in price, not in essence.
3
Differentiate price vs. essence change
The text distinguishes between changes in price (sirf) and changes in the substance (dhat), such as moisture or insect damage. For essence changes, consensus exists: zakat is calculated based on the value at the end of the year, not the beginning.
This distinction limits the scope of the dispute.
4
Note the exceptions
If the entire nisab is destroyed, the year resets completely. Also, if the owner dies mid-year, the heir does not continue the same hawL. Zufar's contrary view (constant nisab throughout) is rejected.
The principle of practicality (istihsan) underlies the majority position.

وإن أدى من القيمة : أدى خمسة دراهم عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: در همين ونصفاً.

وإن كان التغيير إلى زيادة بأن كانت يوم الحول مبتلة، وقيمتها مائتان فیبست حتى صارت تساوي أربعمائة : فإن أدى من العين : فخمسة أقفزة، وإن أدى من القيمة فخمسة دراهم، إجماعاً؛ لأن المستفاد بعد الحول: لا يُضم، ونقصان النصاب: يسقط قدره من الزكاة.

قوله : فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك: لا يُسقط الزكاة: معناه انتقص وبقي البعض، أما إذا هلك كله، واستفاد نصاباً آخر : انقطع حكم النصاب الأول. ولو مات الرجلُ في وسط الحول: انقطع حكم الحول، ولم يَبْنِ
الوارث على ذلك الحول.
Chapter of Zakat on Trade Goods. If the nisab is complete at the two ends of the year, its deficiency in between does not cancel the zakat. If he pays from the value, he pays five dirhams according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two imams, two and a half dirhams. And if this food increased after the year in price until it became worth four hundred, then if he pays from the same, he pays one-tenth of it unanimously. And if he pays from the value, he pays five dirhams according to him, and according to the two, ten dirhams. This is if the increase and decrease are in terms of price. As for if they are in terms of the essence, by means of dryness or moisture or some of it being eaten by moths, so it decreased, as if the wheat became wet after the year until its value became one hundred, while its value at the day of the year was two hundred, or some of it was eaten by moths until it became equal to one hundred: then if he pays from the same, five qafiz, and if he pays from its value, two and a half dirhams, unanimously. And if the change was to an increase, in that at the day of the year it was wet and its value was two hundred, then it dried until it became worth four hundred: then if he pays from the same, five qafiz, and if he pays from the value, five dirhams, unanimously; because what is gained after the year is not combined, and the deficiency of the nisab removes its amount from zakat. * His saying: (And if the nisab is complete at the two ends of the year, its deficiency in between does not cancel the zakat); because it would be difficult to consider completeness during it. As for trade assets, it is apparent because the trader constantly transacts in wealth, and his transaction may be profitable or not with the increase in price and its high cost. And as for grazing animals, they are not free from death and birth, and perhaps some of them are absent. As for the beginning of the year and its end, completeness of the nisab is necessary; at the beginning for the commencement, and at the end for the obligation. And he restricted it with deficiency as a precaution against when all the nisab is destroyed: then the year is cut off by it by agreement. And Zufar said: Zakat is not obligatory for him unless the nisab is complete from the beginning of the year to its end. His saying: Its deficiency in between does not cancel the zakat: its meaning is that it decreases and part remains; but if all of it is destroyed and he acquires another nisab, the ruling of the first nisab is cut off. And if a man dies in the middle of the year, the ruling of the year is cut off, and the heir does not build on that year.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on zakat of trade goods addresses a key ruling: zakat is obligatory if the nisab (minimum threshold) is complete at both the beginning and end of the lunar year, even if it fluctuates below the threshold in between. The commentator first presents the ruling and then explains the scenarios for paying zakat when the value of the goods changes. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding payment from value when the price increases after the year: Abu Hanifa requires payment at the original value (5 dirhams on a 200-dirham nisab), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) require payment at the current value (10 dirhams). However, when the change is in the essence (e.g., wetness, dryness, insect damage), there is consensus that payment from value is based on the value at the end of the year, not the beginning. The commentator also explains the rationale: it is impractical to require the nisab to remain constant throughout the year, as trade goods fluctuate. The passage then addresses exceptions: if the entire nisab is destroyed, the year resets; if the owner dies mid-year, the year is cut off and the heir does not continue it. Zufar's minority view requiring constant nisab throughout the year is noted and rejected.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat. For trade goods, it is the value equivalent to 200 dirhams or 20 mithqals of gold.
حول (ḥawl): The lunar year (around 354 days) that must pass for zakat to become obligatory on owned wealth.
عروض (ʿurūḍ): Trade goods, commodities or merchandise prepared for sale with the intention of profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a trader's goods are worth 200 dirhams at the beginning of the year, drop to 100 dirhams mid-year, and return to 200 dirhams at the end, is zakat obligatory?
A) No, because the nisab was incomplete mid-year.
B) Yes, because the nisab is complete at both ends.
C) Only if the deficit was due to market price change.
D) Only if the trader intended to sell the goods.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods is due when the nisab is complete at the beginning and end of the year; mid-year fluctuations are ignored except in cases of total destruction or death.

Combining Values of Trade Goods with Gold and Silver for Zakat Nisab
Ruling on combining values for zakat nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of combining values of trade goods, gold, and silver to determine when zakat becomes obligatory, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding gold and silver.

Core Idea
In Hanafi zakat, trade goods, gold, and silver are combined by value to reach the nisab — a single wallet view.

This passage from the commentary on the Mukhtasar al-Quduri clarifies a key rule for zakat calculation: different types of wealth can be added together to reach the nisab threshold. The same principle applies when combining gold and silver, though there is a disagreement among the Hanafi imams on whether gold and silver are combined by value. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply this rule correctly and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa from his two students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of wealth mentioned
The passage mentions trade goods (العروض), gold (الذهب), and silver (الفضة). Trade goods are valued at their current market price.
2
Understand the operation of combining (ضم)
Combining means adding the values together to check if the total reaches the nisab (e.g., for silver, 200 dirhams or its equivalent value).
The nisab for gold is 20 mithqal (approx. 85g), for silver 200 dirhams (approx. 595g), or equivalent value.
3
Note the agreed-upon rule
All three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver. So if you have trade goods worth 50 dirhams and silver worth 150 dirhams, the total is 200 dirhams, reaching the nisab.
4
Identify the dispute on gold and silver
Abu Hanifa combines gold and silver by value (e.g., 10 dirhams of gold + 190 dirhams of silver = 200 dirhams → nisab). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not combine them; each is considered separately.
If gold value is less than nisab and silver value is less than nisab, no zakat under their view, even if combined value reaches nisab.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view (combining), as it is more practical.
This is the position taken by later Hanafi authorities such as Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله : ( وتضم قيمة العروض إلى الذهب والفضة).
ـ وكذا يُضم بعضها إلى بعض وإن اختلف أجناسها. -

أبي حنيفة).
And the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver. Likewise, gold is combined with silver by value until the nisab is completed, according to Abu Hanifa. His saying: (And the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver). And similarly, some of them are combined with each other even if their types differ. His saying: (And likewise, gold is combined with silver by value until the nisab is completed, according to Abu Hanifa).
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the Mukhtasar al-Quduri addresses the rules for combining different types of wealth to complete the zakat nisab. The core ruling is that the market value of trade goods (ʿurūḍ) is combined with gold and silver holdings. Similarly, gold and silver are combined by value (not weight) to make up the nisab. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator clarifies that even if the types differ (e.g., different kinds of trade goods, or gold and silver), their values are added together. The phrase 'according to Abu Hanifa' indicates that there is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani do not allow combining gold and silver; each is considered separately. However, for trade goods with gold/silver, there is agreement on combining.

Key Terms
ضم (ḍamm): Combining the value of different types of zakatable wealth (trade goods, gold, silver) to reach the nisab threshold.
العروض (al-ʿurūḍ): Trade goods; items bought and sold for profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about combining gold and silver for zakat nisab?
A) Gold and silver are never combined; each has its own nisab.
B) Gold and silver are combined by weight according to Abu Hanifa.
C) Gold and silver are combined by value according to Abu Hanifa.
D) Gold and silver are combined only if they are of the same purity.

Key Takeaway
Combining values of different zakatable assets is permitted in the Hanafi school, and gold and silver are combined by value according to the mufta bihi position of Abu Hanifa.

Combining Trade Goods and Precious Metals for Zakat: The Value vs. Parts Dispute
Ruling on combining trade goods with gold/silver and intra-Hanafi dispute on combining gold and silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on combining trade goods with gold/silver for zakat nisab and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining gold and silver by value versus by parts.

Core Idea
Zakat nisab for trade goods combines values; gold and silver combine by value only for Abu Hanifa, but by parts for the Sahibayn.

When a trader has multiple types of wealth—trade goods, cash, gold, silver—how do they combine to reach the zakat threshold? This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira presents the general Hanafi rule that the value of trade goods is added to gold and silver, and then dives into a crucial internal disagreement: does gold combine with silver by market value (Abu Hanifa) or by considering fractional shares of their respective nisabs (the Sahibayn)? The answer affects when zakat becomes obligatory. Let's unpack the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule on combining trade goods
Identify the core ruling: the value of trade goods (urud) is combined with gold and silver to complete nisab. Note that different types of trade goods are also combined with each other.
This is the default Hanafi position; it applies to a trader's merchandise.
2
Understand nisab conditions for the zakat year
The passage clarifies that nisab must be complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year. A temporary deficiency in the middle does not cancel zakat, but total destruction of nisab restarts the year. Also, death of the owner cuts the year.
Zufar's stricter view (complete nisab throughout) is rejected.
3
Recognize the dispute on combining gold and silver
Abu Hanifa holds that gold and silver are combined by value (qimah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that they are combined by parts (ajza') – i.e., by considering what fraction of each metal's nisab is owned.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical implications.
4
Analyze the two worked examples
First example: 100 dirhams + 5 mithqals gold worth 100 dirhams → total value 200 dirhams → Abu Hanifa requires zakat, Sahibayn do not (since gold quantity alone is below its nisab). Second example: 10 dinars (worth 50 dirhams) + 100 dirhams → total value 150 dirhams → by parts (half of gold nisab + half of silver nisab = one full nisab) → both require zakat, but for different reasons.
In the second example, Abu Hanifa agrees as a precaution for the poor.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in mixed gold-silver holdings, the method of combining determines whether nisab is reached. A merchant must know which view to follow, as later tarjih often favours Abu Hanifa's value-based approach.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa commonly follows Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn's view remains respected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة العروض. وتُضَمُّ قيمةُ العروض إلى الذهب والفضة . وكذلك يُضَمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة؛ حتى يتم النصاب عند أبي حنيفة . أما في أموال التجارة: فظاهر؛ لأن التاجر دائماً يتصرف في المال، وتصرفه قد يكون رابحاً، وقد لا يكون بازدياد السعر وغلائه. وأما في السوائم : فإنها لا تخلو عن موت وولادة، وربما يغيب بعضها. أما في ابتداء الحول وانتهائه : فلا بد من كمال النصاب، أما في ابتدائه : فللانعقاد، وأما في انتهائه : فللوجوب. - وقيد بالنقصان: احترازاً عما إذا هلك كل النصاب: فإنه ينقطع الحول به بالاتفاق. وقال زفر: لا تلزمه الزكاة، إلا أن يكون النصاب كاملاً من أول الحول إلى آخره. قوله : فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك: لا يُسقط الزكاة: معناه انتقص وبقي البعض، أما إذا هلك كله، واستفاد نصاباً آخر : انقطع حكم النصاب الأول. ولو مات الرجلُ في وسط الحول: انقطع حكم الحول، ولم يَبْنِ الوارث على ذلك الحول. قوله : ( وتُضم قيمة العروض إلى الذهب والفضة). ـ وكذا يُضم بعضها إلى بعض وإن اختلف أجناسها. - قوله: (وكذلك يُضمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة حتى يتم النصاب عند أبي حنيفة). وقالا : لا يُضَمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة، ويُضَمُّ بالأجزاء . كما إذا كان معه مائة درهم، وخمسة مثاقيل قيمتها مائة درهم: فعليه الزكاة عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لهما. قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا يُضمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة، ويُضم بالأجزاء). كما إذا كان معه عشرة دنانير قيمتها خمسون درهماً، ومعه أيضاً مائة درهم وجبت عليه الزكاة عندهما ; لكمال النصاب بالأجزاء، وكذا عنده أيضاً؛ احتياطاً لجهة الفقراء.
Chapter on Zakat of Trade Goods. And the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver. And similarly, gold is combined with silver by value, so that the nisab is completed according to Abu Hanifa. As for trade assets, it is apparent; because the trader constantly transacts with the wealth, and his transaction may be profitable or not due to increase in price and its rise. And as for grazing livestock, they are not free from death and birth, and perhaps some of them are absent. As for the beginning and end of the year: the completion of nisab is necessary—at the beginning for its commencement, and at the end for obligation. And he restricted it with [the word] deficiency, as a precaution against the case when all of the nisab is destroyed: then the year is cut off by it by agreement. Zufar said: Zakat is not obligatory unless the nisab is complete from the beginning of the year to its end. His saying: 'Its deficiency in between does not cancel zakat' means it decreased and some remained; but if it was all destroyed and he acquired another nisab, then the ruling of the first nisab is cut off. If a man dies in the middle of the year, the ruling of the year is cut off, and the heir does not build upon that year. His saying: (And the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver). — And likewise, some of them are combined with others even if their types differ. — His saying: (And similarly, gold is combined with silver by value until the nisab is completed according to Abu Hanifa). And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Gold is not combined with silver by value, but it is combined by parts. For example, if he has one hundred dirhams and five mithqals worth one hundred dirhams, then zakat is due upon him according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Gold is not combined with silver by value, but it is combined by parts). For example, if he has ten dinars worth fifty dirhams, and also one hundred dirhams, then zakat is due upon him according to them (the Sahibayn) due to completion of nisab by parts; and also according to him (Abu Hanifa), out of precaution for the sake of the poor.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira presents the ruling on combining different types of wealth to complete the nisab for zakat of trade goods (urud al-tijarah), along with the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining gold and silver by value or by parts. The author first states the general rule: the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver; likewise, gold is combined with silver by value to complete the nisab according to Imam Abu Hanifa. He then provides reasoning: for trade goods, it is obvious because the merchant constantly deals with the wealth, and profit may or may not occur due to price fluctuations. For grazing livestock, the ruling is similar because animals are subject to death and birth. However, for the beginning and end of the zakat year, completion of nisab is required—at the beginning to initiate the year, and at the end for obligation. A deficiency in the middle does not cancel zakat, as long as some of the nisab remains; if the entire nisab is destroyed, the year is cut off, and if new nisab is acquired, a new year begins. If the owner dies mid-year, the year is cut off, and the heir does not continue that year. The text then returns to the main ruling: trade goods of different types are combined with each other. Then it details the dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that gold and silver are combined by value to complete nisab, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that they are combined by parts (i.e., by weight/quantity, not by value). The first example: a person has 100 dirhams (silver) and 5 mithqals of gold worth 100 dirhams—total value 200 dirhams—so zakat is due according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn because each metal's quantity alone is below its respective nisab and they are not combined by value. In the second example: 10 dinars (gold) worth 50 dirhams and 100 dirhams (silver)—total value 150 dirhams. According to the Sahibayn, zakat is due because the quantities of gold and silver, when considered as fractions of their respective nisabs (half of gold nisab and half of silver nisab), combine to complete one full nisab. Surprisingly, Abu Hanifa also agrees in this specific case, as a precaution for the poor. The passage thus illustrates the nuanced positions within the Hanafi school on the method of combining gold and silver for zakat purposes.

Key Terms
عروض (urud): Trade goods (merchandise) intended for sale.
ضم (damm): Combining different categories of wealth for nisab completion.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat: 200 dirhams silver or equivalent.
القيمة (al-qimah): Market value, used by Abu Hanifa to combine gold and silver.
الأجزاء (al-ajza'): Fractions of nisab based on weight/quantity of gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By their physical weight (parts)
B) By their market value
C) They are not combined at all
D) Only gold is considered

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits combining trade goods with gold and silver by value; for gold and silver themselves, there is a significant internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa (by value) and the Sahibayn (by parts), with practical consequences for zakat calculation.

Combining Gold and Silver for Zakat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on combining gold and silver by value vs. parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining gold and silver for zakat nisab, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Gold and silver can be combined for zakat, but the method—by value or by weight—is a key intra-Hanafi dispute.

The Hanafi school recognizes a valid disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding how gold and silver are combined to reach the zakat threshold. The source passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira sets out the dispute clearly, with examples showing when zakat becomes due under each view. This lesson unpacks the arguments and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage states that Abu Hanifa allows combining gold and silver by their market value (قيمة), while the Sahibayn only allow combining by weight/parts (أجزاء). Note the key terms.
2
Examine the examples given
Two scenarios illustrate the difference: (1) 100 dirhams and 5 mithqals worth 100 dirhams: under Abu Hanifa, value totals 200 dirhams, so zakat is due; under Sahibayn, neither metal reaches its own nisab, so no zakat. (2) 10 dinars worth 50 dirhams and 100 dirhams: both agree zakat is due because the combined weight (10 mithqals + 100 dirhams?) actually in this example, the text says 'nisab is completed by parts' – careful: here the combined weight reaches the nisab, so both agree.
The second example shows that when the actual weights combine to reach a nisab (e.g., 10 mithqals of gold plus silver weight?), the ruling is unanimous.
3
Understand the basis of each view
The Sahibayn rely on the fact that zakat on gold and silver is measured by weight based on hadith (20 mithqal gold, 200 dirhams silver). Abu Hanifa argues that since both are mediums of exchange, value is relevant, and adopting value-based combination is a precaution for the poor (احتياطاً لجهة الفقراء).
This illustrates a common pattern: Abu Hanifa often employs istihsan and precaution, while the Sahibayn stick to qiyas and literal weight.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person has gold below 20 mithqal but its value brings the total value of gold+silver to 200 dirhams, Abu Hanifa deems zakat wajib; the Sahibayn do not. The mufta bihi today is the Sahibayn's view, but precaution suggests giving zakat as per Abu Hanifa.
This is a classic case where the mufti can advise the cautious route.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة العروض
وقالا : لا يُضَمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة، ويُضَمُّ بالأجزاء .
كما إذا كان معه مائة درهم، وخمسة مثاقيل قيمتها مائة درهم: فعليه الزكاة عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لهما.
قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا يُضمُّ الذهب إلى الفضة بالقيمة، ويُضم بالأجزاء).
كما إذا كان معه عشرة دنانير قيمتها خمسون درهماً، ومعه أيضاً مائة درهم وجبت عليه الزكاة عندهما ؛ لكمال النصاب بالأجزاء، وكذا عنده أيضاً؛ احتياطاً لجهة الفقراء.
Chapter on Zakat of Trade Goods. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Gold is not combined with silver by value, but is combined by parts. For example, if someone has one hundred dirhams and five mithqals worth one hundred dirhams: then zakat is due according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. His statement: (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Gold is not combined with silver by value, but is combined by parts). For example, if someone has ten dinars worth fifty dirhams, and also one hundred dirhams, zakat is due according to them because the nisab is completed by parts, and also according to him (Abu Hanifa) as a precaution for the sake of the poor.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage addresses a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the combination (ضم) of gold and silver for the purpose of completing the nisab (minimum threshold) for zakat. The matn states the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn): gold and silver are not to be combined based on their market value (قيمة), but rather based on their weight (أجزاء), meaning by the actual weight of each metal. Abu Hanifa, however, allows combining them by value. The commentary provides two examples to illustrate the difference. In the first example, a person has 100 dirhams (silver) and 5 mithqals of gold worth 100 dirhams. According to Abu Hanifa, because the value of the gold completes the silver nisab (200 dirhams), zakat is due. The Sahibayn disagree because they combine only by weight, not by value. In the second example, a person has 10 dinars (gold) worth 50 dirhams and 100 dirhams (silver). Here, both parties agree that zakat is due because the weight of the gold (10 mithqals) combined with the silver weight reaches a combined nisab? Actually the text says 'لكمال النصاب بالأجزاء' meaning the nisab is completed by parts (weight). The commentary notes that this is a precaution for the benefit of the poor. The dispute is a practical one: the mufta bihi position today is that gold and silver are not combined for zakat, following the Sahibayn, but the precautionary practice may follow Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
ضم الذهب إلى الفضة (ḍamm al-dhahab ilā al-fiḍḍah): Combining gold with silver for the purpose of completing the nisab for zakat.
القيمة (al-qīmah): Market value; used to combine gold and silver by their worth rather than weight.
النصاب (al-niṣāb): The minimum threshold of wealth that obligates zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), how should gold and silver be combined for zakat nisab?
A) By their market value (قيمة)
B) By their weight (أجزاء)
C) Not combined at all
D) Only if they are of the same type

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits combining gold and silver for zakat nisab, but the method—by value (Abu Hanifa) or by weight (Sahibayn)—is a practical intra-madhhab dispute with different outcomes.

Abu Hanifa's Ruling on 'Ushr: All Produce Obligates the Tithe
States ruling and conditions of 'ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling that 'ushr is wajib on all produce of 'ushri land, identify the minimum threshold as one sa', and distinguish this from the Sahibayn's requirement of nisab.

Core Idea
No harvest too small: in Abu Hanifa's school, every grain of 'ushri land carries the tithe.

In this passage, the commentator of Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyirah begins the chapter on zakat of crops by clarifying that the term 'zakat' here refers to the 'ushr (tithe). He then presents Abu Hanifa's distinctive ruling: the 'ushr is due on all produce of 'ushri land, whether little or much, regardless of the owner's legal capacity or the land's waqf status. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the key intra-madhhab disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The core matn states: 'On little and much of what the earth produces: the tithe.' The commentator adds that the minimum is one sa' (or half sa' according to some).
This is Abu Hanifa's position, distinct from other schools.
2
Understand the scope
The obligation applies to all produce from 'ushri land, regardless of quantity, and irrespective of who owns the land (adult, child, slave, or waqf). The land must be 'ushri, not kharaji.
The commentary explicitly says 'no attention is paid to the owner'.
3
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require nisab (5 wasaq) and continuity for the obligation, unlike Abu Hanifa.
This difference affects the definition: Sahibayn call it zakat because of nisab and continuity, while Abu Hanifa calls it zakat because of the same recipients.
4
Recognize the conditions
Key conditions: land must be 'ushriyyah, and produce must reach the minimum threshold (one sa' preferred). If the land is kharajiyyah, no 'ushr is due.
The minimum threshold is debated: some say half sa'.
5
Apply the ruling
Today, this means even a small harvest from a backyard orchard on 'ushri land obligates the tithe, unlike the Sahibayn's view.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position, being more precautionary.

Chapter on Zakat of Crops and Fruits. Abu Hanifa said: On little and much of what the earth produces: the tithe ('ushr), whether it is irrigated by flowing water. Chapter on Zakat of Crops and Fruits. What is meant by zakat here is the 'ushr, and its being called zakat is according to their (Sahibayn's) usage because they require nisab and continuity, so it is a type of zakat. Similarly according to Abu Hanifa, because its expenditure is the same as zakat, it is called zakat. Al-`ushr). He (the author) said: (Abu Hanifa said: On little and much of what the earth produces: the tithe). The definition of little: one sa', and what is less than that: nothing on it. And it is said: its limit is half a sa'. What is meant by land here is 'ushri land, and it contains an indication that no attention is paid to the owner, whether he is an adult, child, insane, slave, or if the land is a waqf for ribats, mosques, or schools. * His statement: (whether irrigated by flowing water): 'sayh' means running water.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zakat of crops and fruits (زكاة الزروع والثمار). The commentator begins by clarifying that the term 'zakat' in this chapter actually refers to the 'ushr (tithe), not the usual zakat on wealth. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) call it zakat because they require nisab and continuity (بقاء), making it similar to zakat. Abu Hanifa also calls it zakat because the recipients are the same as zakat. The core matn states Abu Hanifa's famous position: the 'ushr is due on all produce of the earth, whether little or much, regardless of the quantity. This is a distinctive Hanafi view. The commentary then explains the minimum threshold: some say the minimum that obligates 'ushr is one sa' (approximately 2.5 liters), and below that there is no obligation; others say half a sa'. The land in question is 'ushri land (land conquered by treaty or owned by Muslims), as opposed to kharaji land (tax land). Importantly, the obligation of 'ushr is on the produce, not on the owner, so it applies even if the owner is a child, madman, slave, or if the land is waqf. This is because the produce itself is subject to the right of Allah. The commentary also explains the phrase 'whether irrigated by flowing water' (سقي سيحاً), noting that 'sayh' means running water, which is contrasted with water lifted by machine or rain, but the implication is that the 'ushr is applicable regardless of irrigation method, though the rate may differ (the text here does not mention the rate difference, just that the same rule applies).

Key Terms
العشر (al-‘ushr): The tithe (one-tenth) due on agricultural produce of 'ushri land.
الأرض العشرية (al-arḍ al-‘ushriyyah): Land conquered by treaty or owned by Muslims, subject to 'ushr rather than kharaj.
الصاع (al-ṣā‘): A unit of volume equal to approximately 2.5 liters; used here as the minimum amount of produce to obligate ‘ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum amount of produce that obligates 'ushr according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Five wasaq
B) One sa'
C) Half a sa'
D) Any amount regardless of size

Key Takeaway
According to Abu Hanifa, the 'ushr is wajib on every harvest from 'ushri land, regardless of the quantity, as long as it reaches one sa'.

Zakat on Crops: The Ruling of 'Ushr According to Abu Hanifa
States Abu Hanifa's ruling on 'ushr for land produce and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on 'ushr for land produce, identify the exceptions, and explain the threshold for 'little'.

Core Idea
On any produce of the land, little or much, the tithe is due—except for plants not normally cultivated.

This passage presents Abu Hanifa's foundational ruling on zakat of crops. Unlike zakat on wealth, 'ushr is not subject to a minimum quantity (nisab) nor a year's holding. The rulings are detailed with exceptions and clarifications that are essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal ruling (hukm) for agricultural produce according to Abu Hanifa?
Note that it is obligatory (fard 'ayn) on any amount.
2
Recognize the irrigation method
Does the method of irrigation affect the obligation?
The text states it applies whether irrigated by a stream or rain.
3
List the exceptions
Which items are exempt from 'ushr and why?
The exceptions are firewood, sugarcane, grass, palm fronds, and straw.
4
Understand the threshold
What is defined as 'little' that is exempt from 'ushr?
The threshold is one sa' (about 2.5 kg) or half a sa' according to some.
5
Consider the owner's status
Does the legal capacity or type of ownership affect the obligation?
It applies regardless of owner being adult, child, insane, slave, or waqf.

- وكذا التبن : لا شيء فيه أيضاً ؛ لأنه ساق الحبوب، كالشجر للثمار، ولأن المقصود غيرهما، وهو الثمر والحب، وأما إذا قصد بالشجر: الاستغلال كشجر السرح: فإنه يجب فيه العشر.
Chapter of Zakat of Crops and Fruits. Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: On the little of what the land produces and its much: the tithe (al-‘ushr), whether it is irrigated by a stream or the sky waters it, except firewood, sugarcane, and grass. The intent of zakat here is the tithe, and calling it zakat is in accordance with their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view, because they stipulate the nisab and annual lapse, so it is a type of zakat. Likewise according to Abu Hanifa, because its distribution is the same as zakat, it is called zakat. The definition of little: a sa' ; what is less than that has nothing in it. And it is said: its limit is half a sa'. And the intent of the land here is the 'ushri land, and it contains an indication that attention is not paid to the owner, whether he is an adult, a child, an insane person, a slave, or the land is a waqf for ribat, mosques, or schools. His saying: (whether it is irrigated by a stream) meaning flowing water. His saying: (or the sky waters it) meaning rain, Allah Most High said: 'And We sent the sky upon them continuously.' (Al-An'am 6:6). And the poet said: 'When the sky descends upon a land of people, we pasture on it even if they are angry.' His saying: (except firewood, sugarcane, and grass); because these items are not normally cultivated, rather they remain on the ground. And likewise palm fronds: nothing is due on them because they are from the branches of trees, and there is no tithe on trees. And likewise straw: nothing is due on it also, because it is the stalk of grains, like the tree for fruits, and because the purpose is other than them, which is the fruit and grain. But if one intends the tree for exploitation, like the shajar al-sarh, then the tithe is obligatory.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on zakat of crops and fruits. The author states Abu Hanifa's ruling that the tithe (al-‘ushr) is obligatory on both little and much of what the land produces, regardless of how it is irrigated—whether by a stream (sayh) or by rain. The only exceptions are firewood (hatab), sugarcane (qasab), and grass (hashish). The commentary then clarifies that the term 'zakat' here means 'ushr, and it is called zakat because its recipients are the same as zakat recipients, even though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require nisab and annual lapse for it to be called zakat; Abu Hanifa does not require nisab for land produce but still calls it zakat due to the similarity in distribution. Next, the author explains the definition of 'little' (qalil): most scholars say it is one sa' (approximately 2.5 kg), and nothing is due on less than that; some say half a sa'. The land referred to is 'ushri land (taxed at 10%). The owner's status (adult, child, insane, slave) does not matter, nor does the type of ownership (private or waqf). The commentary then explains the two irrigation methods: sayh (flowing water) and rain, and confirms that both incur the same 'ushr. The exceptions are justified because these plants are not normally cultivated; they are left on the ground. Additionally, palm fronds (sa'f) and straw (tibn) are exempt because they are analogous to tree branches and grain stalks, respectively. However, if trees are cultivated for their leaves (like al-sarh), then 'ushr is due on them.

Key Terms
العُشْر (al-‘ushr): The tithe (10%) on agricultural produce, obligatory as zakat.
السَّيْح (al-sayh): Flowing water used for irrigation.
القليل (al-qalil): Less than one sa' (approximately 2.5 kg), the minimum threshold for 'ushr according to the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wheat
B) Firewood
C) Barley
D) Dates

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa rules that 'ushr is obligatory on any amount of cultivated land produce, regardless of irrigation, but excludes plants not normally cultivated.

Types of Sugarcane and Their Zakat Rulings
Classification of sugarcane types and their 'ushr rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of qasab and identify which are subject to 'ushr based on their agricultural use.

Core Idea
Only sugar cane and dhirah cane (grain-producing) are subject to 'ushr; Persian cane is exempt.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the Hanafi tradition that distinguishes between three types of sugarcane. The key is understanding that 'ushr is imposed on cultivated produce intended for human consumption, which helps explain why only certain types are taxable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
List the three types of qasab as mentioned: sugar cane (qasab al-sukkar), dhirah cane (qasab al-dhirah, also called spike cane), and Persian cane (qasab al-farsi).
Dhirah cane is defined as 'the cane of the ear', meaning it produces grain.
2
Note the ruling for each type
The text states that sugar cane and dhirah cane have the 'ushr upon them. Persian cane is not mentioned, implying it is exempt.
The ruling is based on the general principle that 'ushr applies to produce that is cultivated and used for sustenance.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The 'ushr is due on crops that are intentionally cultivated for human consumption. Dhirah cane yields grains like wheat, so it qualifies. Persian cane, likely used for fodder or other purposes, does not trigger 'ushr.
4
Apply the rule
If a farmer grows both sugar cane and Persian cane, he pays 'ushr only on the sugar cane. This shows the need to classify the crop before applying zakat.

The author identifies three types: sugar cane (qasab al-sukkar), dhirah cane (qasab al-dhirah) which is also called spike cane (qasab al-sunbul), and Persian cane (qasab al-farsi). The ruling is that sugar cane and dhirah cane are subject to the tithe (al-‘ushr), while Persian cane is not. The author also identifies dhirah (ذَريرة) as the cane of the ear (sunbul), which is a type of cane that produces grains like wheat. This aligns with the principle that only cultivated produce intended for human consumption is subject to 'ushr.

Key Terms

العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe, a zakat obligation of one-tenth on certain agricultural produce.

The Lasting Fruit Condition in Zakat on Crops: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Commentary on matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri with intra-Hanafi dispute on lasting fruit condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the lasting fruit condition for tithe (ushr) and apply the mufta bihi ruling to specific crops.

Core Idea
Tithe is wajib on all cultivated crops for Abu Hanifa; only on storable staples for the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the obligation of tithe on crops. While the general ruling is that rain-watered land yields a tenth, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) impose an additional condition: the produce must have a 'lasting fruit' that can be stored for a year without special effort. Abu Hanifa disagrees, leading to different practical applications. By understanding this dispute, you will learn how interpretive principles shape fiqh rulings and which position is considered mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exceptions
The matn states that rain-watered crops are liable for tithe except firewood, reed, and grass. Note that these exceptions are based on non-cultivation.
The exceptions are not subject to tithe because they are not normally cultivated.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's condition
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require 'thamar baqiya' (lasting fruit) — produce that remains in its original state for a year without preservation or drying. They list examples such as wheat, barley, dates, raisins, etc.
Perishable items like onions and garlic are excluded under this view.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's broader view
Abu Hanifa does not require lasting fruit; tithe applies to any cultivated crop intended for food or general benefit. His view is supported by the general proofs of zakat on crops.
This view is more inclusive, covering vegetables and perishables.
4
Compare the practical outcomes
Under Sahibayn, onions and garlic would not be subject to tithe because they perish; under Abu Hanifa, they are. The commentator states that tithe is obligatory on walnuts, almonds, onions, and garlic 'in the sound position' (al-sahih), indicating Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon.
The sound position (al-sahih) is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator favors Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the inclusion of onions and garlic. Thus, the operative ruling is that tithe is due on all cultivated crops intended for food or general benefit, regardless of storability.
This is consistent with the broader Hanafi principle of encouraging social welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الزروع والثمار
أو سَقَتْه السماء، إلا الحطب، والقصب، والحشيش.
* قوله: (أو سقته السماء): يعني المطر، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَأَرْسَلْنَا السَّمَاءَ عَلَيْهِم مِّدْرَارًا . الأنعام /٦ .

إذا وقع السماء بأرض قوم رعيناها وإن كانوا غضاباً

- وكذا السعف : لا شيء فيه؛ لأنه من أغصان الشجر، والشجر لا عُشر فيه.
- وكذا التبن : لا شيء فيه أيضاً ؛ لأنه ساق الحبوب، كالشجر للثمار، ولأن المقصود غيرهما، وهو الثمر والحب، وأما إذا قصد بالشجر: الاستغلال كشجر السرح: فإنه يجب فيه العشر.

وقالا : لا يجب العشر إلا فيما له ثمرة باقية،
وأما القصب الفارسي: فلا شيء فيه؛ لأنه لا يستنبت.
وهذا إذا كان في أطراف الأرض، أما إذا اتخذ أرضه مَقصَبَةً، أو مشجرة، أو منبتاً للحشيش، أو ساق إليه الماء، ومنع الناس منه: يجب فيه العشر.
قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا يجب العشر إلا فيما له ثمرةً باقية).
أي تبقى عينه حولاً من غير تكلُّف، ولا تشميس، مما يقتات، كالحنطة والشعير والذرة والدخن والأرز والجاورس والعدس والماش واللوبيا، الدخن، والحمص والبرعي والهندباء والتمر والزبيب، وما أشبه ذلك مما يُقصد به الأكل، وهو يبقى سنةً، أو يُنتفع به انتفاعاً عاماً، كالزعفران والعصفر والفلفل والكمون والخردل والكزبرة: ففيه العشر.
وفي السمسم : العُشر، فإن عُصر قبل أن يؤخذ منه العشر: أخذ من دهنه، ولم يؤخذ من الشجيرة شيء.
وكذا الزيتون على هذا.
ويجب العشر في الجوز واللوز والبصل والثوم، في الصحيح.
ولا عُشر في الأدوية، كالسعتر والشونيز والحلف والحلبة.
Chapter of Zakat of Crops and Fruits.
Or if the sky watered it, except firewood, reed, and grass.
* His statement: 'or if the sky watered it' means rain. Allah ta'ala said: 'And We sent the sky upon them in abundant rain.' (Al-An'am 6)
And the poet said: 'When the sky falls upon the land of a people, we graze it even if they are angry.'
His statement: 'except firewood, reed, and grass' because these things are not normally cultivated; rather, they remain on the ground.
- Likewise, palm leaves: nothing is due on them because they are branches of the tree, and there is no tithe on trees.
- Likewise, chaff: nothing is due on it as well, because it is the stalk of grains, like the tree for fruits, and because the intended thing is other than them, namely the fruit and grain. And if one intends the tree for exploitation, like the tree of arak (Salvadora persica), then tithe is obligatory on it.
As for reed: it is three types: sugarcane, fragrant reed (qasab al-dharīra), and Persian reed.
Sugarcane and fragrant reed: tithe is due on both. Al-dharīra is the reed of ear of grain?
And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Tithe is not obligatory except on that which has a lasting fruit.
As for Persian reed: nothing is due on it because it is not cultivated.
This is when it is on the edges of the land; if one takes his land as a reed-plot, or as a tree-plot, or as a growing ground for grass, or channels water to it and prevents people from it, then tithe is obligatory.
His statement: 'Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Tithe is not obligatory except on that which has a lasting fruit' i.e., whose substance remains for a year without effort or drying, such as wheat, barley, corn, millet, rice, jawarse (a grain like maize), lentils, mung beans, cowpeas, millet, chickpeas, lupine, endive, dates, raisins, and the like from what is intended for eating and remains for a year, or from which there is general benefit, like saffron, safflower, pepper, cumin, mustard, coriander: then tithe is due on it.
And on sesame: tithe is due; if it is pressed before taking the tithe, then the tithe is taken from its oil, and nothing is taken from the plant.
Likewise, olives on this.
And tithe is obligatory on walnuts, almonds, onions, and garlic, according to the sound position.
There is no tithe on medicinal items, like thyme, black cumin, anise, and fenugreek.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri regarding zakat on crops and fruits. It begins by stating the general rule: crops watered by rain are subject to tithe (ushr), but there are exceptions: firewood, reed, and grass are exempt because they are not normally cultivated but grow wild. The commentator clarifies that 'sky' here means rain, citing a Quranic verse and a poetic line for linguistic illustration.

The commentary then addresses additional exempt items: palm leaves (sa'af) and chaff (tibn) are not subject to tithe because they are not the primary goal of cultivation; the fruit and grain are. However, if trees are explicitly cultivated for their leaves or other uses, like the arak tree used for toothbrushes, then tithe becomes obligatory.

Regarding reed (qasab), three types are distinguished: sugarcane and fragrant reed (qasab al-dharīra) are subject to tithe because they are cultivated and have valuable produce. Persian reed, which is not cultivated, is exempt. This ruling applies when these plants grow naturally on the edges of land; if one intentionally cultivates them by dedicating land and watering, then tithe is due.

The passage then presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that tithe is only obligatory on crops that have a 'lasting fruit' (thamara bāqiya) – i.e., produce that remains intact for a year without special preservation or drying. They list examples: wheat, barley, corn, millet, rice, lentils, beans, dates, raisins, etc., and also items with general benefit like saffron, pepper, cumin, etc. This contrasts with Abu Hanifa's position, which does not require the produce to be storable; rather, tithe is due on any crop that is cultivated and yields food or general benefit. The commentator then gives rulings on sesame (tithe taken from oil if pressed), olives (same), and the sound position on walnuts, almonds, onions, and garlic being subject to tithe. Finally, medicinal plants like thyme, black cumin, and fenugreek are exempt.

Key Terms
العشر (al-‘ushr): The tithe (one-tenth) due on crops and fruits irrigated by rain or natural sources; it is a form of zakat.
القصب (al-qasab): Reed; in this text, three types: sugarcane, fragrant reed (qasab al-dharīra), and Persian reed. The first two are subject to tithe, the last is not because it is not cultivated.
ثمرة باقية (thamara bāqiya): A lasting fruit – produce that remains in its original state for a year without special preservation or drying, and is usually stored as food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the obligation of 'ushr?
A) 'Ushr is obligatory on all cultivated crops regardless of their nature.
B) 'Ushr is obligatory only on crops that have a lasting fruit (thamara bāqiya).
C) 'Ushr is not obligatory on any crop, only on livestock.
D) 'Ushr is obligatory only on crops watered by rain.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that tithe is obligatory on all cultivated crops intended for food or general benefit, regardless of storability, following Abu Hanifa's view.
