Zakat on Honey: No Nisab Required in the Hanafi School
States ruling on zakat for honey with narrative evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for honey and identify the evidence from the Sunnah that supports the absence of nisab.

Core Idea
Honey from 'ushr land is subject to 'ushr from the first drop — no nisab.

This lesson addresses a unique zakat ruling: honey, unlike agricultural produce, is not subject to the standard nisab of 5 wasqs. The Hanafi school holds that 'ushr is due on any amount of honey harvested from 'ushr land. This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab, as transmitted in a hadith. We will examine the text, the evidence, and the reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that 'ushr is due on honey from 'ushr land, whether little or much. Note the absence of any minimum quantity.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a historical account (athar) of Banu Shababa and Umar's letter. Identify the key figures and the narrative.
The account is found in al-Nihaya and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet accepted one qirbah from every ten, without mentioning a lower limit. This establishes a ratio without a nisab threshold.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school requires a nisab of 5 wasqs by analogy to crops. The Hanafi position relies on the specific sunnah overriding qiyas.
5
Understand the reasoning
The commentator mentions that bees eat from flowers and fruits, so honey is akin to produce. However, the specific sunnah takes precedence over general analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي العسل : العُشْرُ إِذا أُخِذَ من أرض العُشْرِ، قَلَّ أو كثر . لما روي أن بني شَبَابَة - بفتح الشين - قوم من خثعم بالطائف، كانت لهم نحل، وكانوا يؤدون من عَسَلِها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كل عشر قُرَب : قُربة، وكان يحمي لهم وادي. فلما كان في زمن عمر رضي الله عنه استعمل عليهم سفيان بن عبد الله الثقفي، فأبوا أن يعطوه شيئاً من العسل، فكتب إلى عمر رضي الله عنه بذلك، فكتب إليه عمر: إن النحل ذُبَابُ غَيْث يسوقه الله تعالى إلى مَن يشاء، فإن أدوا إليك ما كانوا يؤدونه إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاحم لهم واديهم، وإلا : فخَل بينهم وبين الناس، فدفعوا إليه حينئذ العشر منه»(۱). كذا في «النهاية». والمعنى فيه : أن النحل يأكل من أنوار الشجر، ومن ثمارها، كما قال الله تعالى: ثم كلي مِن كُلِّ الثَّمَرَتِ . النحل / ٦٩.
And regarding honey: the 'ushr (is due) if taken from 'ushr land, whether little or much. Because it is narrated that Banu Shababa - with a fatha on the shin - a tribe of Khath'am in Ta'if, had bees, and they used to give from its honey to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) one qirbah out of every ten qirbahs, and he would protect their valley. When in the time of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) he appointed Sufyan ibn Abdullah al-Thaqafi over them, they refused to give him any honey. So he wrote to Umar about that, and Umar wrote to him: 'Indeed, bees are flies of rain that Allah sends to whom He wills. If they give you what they used to give to the Messenger of Allah, then protect their valley; otherwise, leave them and the people.' So they then paid the 'ushr from it. Thus in al-Nihaya. And the meaning in it: that bees eat from the blossoms of trees and from their fruits, as Allah Almighty said: 'Then eat from all the fruits' (Surah al-Nahl, 69).
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on honey: 'ushr is due when honey is taken from 'ushr land (land subject to 'ushr tax), regardless of the quantity (whether little or much). This is a unique ruling because unlike most crops, honey does not have a nisab of 5 wasqs; it is subject to 'ushr from the first drop. The evidence is a historical hadith about the tribe Banu Shababa in Ta'if who had bees. They used to give one qirbah (a large water skin) for every ten qirbahs to the Prophet (s), and he would protect their valley from others (as a form of pasture reserve). When Umar was caliph, the governor Sufyan ibn Abdullah wrote that they refused to pay. Umar replied with a letter stating that bees are like rain—divinely provided—and if they pay the same as they did to the Prophet, protect their valley; otherwise, let people take the honey. They then paid the 'ushr. The commentator notes that this report is found in al-Nihaya (a Hanafi fiqh source). The reasoning (معنى) is that bees eat from flowers and fruits of trees, so their product is akin to produce of the land, thus subject to 'ushr. Allah's verse (16:69) instructs bees to eat from all fruits, indicating the source of honey.

Key Terms
أرض العشر (arḍ al-'ushr): Land that is subject to 'ushr tax (as opposed to kharaj land); typically owned by Muslims and not conquered by force.
القربة (al-qirbah): A large water skin used as a measure for honey; one qirbah out of ten.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the nisab for honey according to the Hanafi school?
A) 5 wasqs like other crops.
B) 5 mann.
C) No nisab; 'ushr is due on any amount.
D) 10 qirbahs.

Key Takeaway
Honey from 'ushr land is subject to 'ushr of 1/10 without any minimum quantity, based on the sunnah of the Prophet and Umar.

Zakat on Saffron: Five Mann Nisab
A concise ruling setting the nisab for saffron.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for zakat on saffron according to the Hanafi school and explain the weight conversions of the mann.

Core Idea
Saffron's zakat threshold is five mann, measured by weight, not volume.

This lesson clarifies that saffron, a valuable spice, has a specific minimum amount (nisab) for zakat. Unlike grains measured by volume, saffron is weighed. The Hanafi school sets this threshold at five mann, and the text also defines the mann in terms of uqiyas, mithqals, and dirhams, ensuring precise calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commodity and its nisab
Locate the phrase 'وفي الزعفران : خمسة أمناء' and note that the nisab for saffron is five mann.
The word أمناء is the plural of منّ.
2
Understand the weight system
The text breaks down the mann: 1 mann = 26 uqiyas; 1 uqiya = 7 mithqals = 10 dirhams. Calculate the total dirhams: 5 mann × 26 uqiyas/mann × 10 dirhams/uqiya = 1300 dirhams ≈ 812.5 grams.
This weight is specific to saffron; other commodities have different nisab measurements.
3
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Recognize that the Hanafi school specifies a weight-based nisab for saffron, while other schools may not have a specific nisab or may assess zakat on value alone.
This difference can affect practical zakat calculations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الزعفران : خمسة أمناء . (وفي الزعفران خمسة أمنان) ، والمَنُ: ستة وعشرون أوقية، والأوقية: سبعة مثاقيل، وهي عشرة دراهم.
And regarding saffron: five mann. (And regarding saffron, five mann,) and the mann is twenty-six uqiyas, and the uqiya is seven mithqals, and it is ten dirhams.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a concise ruling statement from the matn, specifying the minimum amount (nisab) for zakat on saffron. The text states that zakat becomes due when one possesses five mann of saffron. The commentator then clarifies the weight measurements: a mann equals twenty-six uqiyas, each uqiya equals seven mithqals, and each mithqal equals ten dirhams. This establishes a precise weight standard unique to saffron and similar commodities, as opposed to general crops where nisab is measured by volume (e.g., five wasq).

Key Terms
مَنّ (mann): A unit of weight equal to 26 uqiyas, equivalent to approx. 260 dirhams or roughly 812.5 grams based on standard Hanafi weights.

Zakat on Honey: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute Over Nisab
Establishes the ruling of zakat on honey and presents the disagreement among Hanafi imams on the minimum amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat of honey, identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding nisab, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each position.

Core Idea
Honey from tithe land is subject to ushr, but the Hanafi imams differ on whether a minimum amount is required before zakat is due.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira establishes the ruling that honey from tithe land incurs ushr, drawing from prophetic practice and analogy to fruits. However, the three major Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—disagree on whether a nisab (minimum threshold) applies. Understanding this dispute highlights how analogical reasoning (qiyas) and practical considerations can lead to different conclusions within a single school.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling and its basis
Identify the core ruling: ushr (10%) is wajib on honey from tithe land. Note the hadith proof from the Prophet and Caliph ‘Umar.
The hadith is cited as evidence that honey is zakatable.
2
Understand the analogy to fruits
The commentator explains that bees eat from blossoms and fruits, so honey is derived from fruits; thus it shares the ruling of fruits on tithe land (ushr).
This qiyas is the primary legal reasoning.
3
Identify the dispute on nisab
Abu Hanifa says no nisab; any amount is zakatable. Abu Yusuf requires ten ziqaq (500 mann). Muhammad requires five afraq (180 Iraqi ratls).
All three are Hanafi imams; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Compare the rationales
Abu Hanifa analogizes honey to fruits which have no nisab. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad likely analogize to other zakatable commodities that have thresholds.
The text does not give their explicit dalil, but it can be inferred.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view (no nisab). Some later scholars adopt a de minimis threshold for practicality.
The mufta bihi is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وفي العسل : العُشْرُ ، قل أو كثر إذا أُخذ من أرض العشر). لما روي أن بني شَبَابَة - بفتح الشين - قوم من خثعم بالطائف، كانت لهم نحل، وكانوا يؤدون من عَسَلِها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كل عشر قُرَب : قُربة، وكان يحمي لهم واديهم. فلما كان في زمن عمر رضي الله عنه استعمل عليهم سفيان بن عبد الله الثقفي، فأبوا أن يعطوه شيئاً من العسل، فكتب إلى عمر رضي الله عنه بذلك، فكتب إليه عمر: إن النحل ذُبَابُ غَيْث يسوقه الله تعالى إلى مَن يشاء، فإن أدوا إليك ما كانوا يؤدونه إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاحم لهم واديهم، وإلا : فخَل بينهم وبين الناس، فدفعوا إليه حينئذ العشر منه». كذا في «النهاية». والمعنى فيه : أن النحل يأكل من أنوار الشجر، ومن ثمارها، كما قال الله تعالى: ثم كلي مِن كُلِّ الثَّمَرَتِ . النحل / ٦٩. والعسل متولد من الثمار، وفي الثمار إذا كانت في الأرض العشرية: العشر، فكذا ما يتولد منها. وأما إذا كانت الأرض خراجية : لم يجب فيها شيء؛ لأن ثمارها لم يجب فيها عشر. وبهذا فارق دودَ القَزّ: فإنه يأكل الورق، دون الثمار، وليس في الأوراق شيء، فكذا ما يتولد منها، والذي يتولد من دود القز: هو الإبريسم، ولا عُشر فيه ؛ لما ذكرنا. ثم عند أبي حنيفة يجب العشر في العسل، قل أو كثر؛ لأنه يجري مجرى الثمار، والعشر عنده يجب في قليل الثمار وكثيرها؛ لأنه لا يُعتبر فيها النصاب. * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف : لا شيء فيه حتى يبلغ عشرة أزقاق)، كل رق: خمسون منا، و مجموعه : خمسمائة من. قوله: (وقال محمد : خمسة أفراق، والفرق: ستة وثلاثون رطلاً بالعراقي). الفرق: بفتحتين: إناء يأخذ ستة عشر رطلاً. كذا في «المستصفى»، والمحدثون يسكنون الراء.
(And regarding honey: one-tenth, whether little or much, if taken from tithe land). Because it is narrated that the Banu Shababa—with a fatha on the shin—a tribe of Khath‘am in Ta’if, had bees, and they used to pay from its honey to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from every ten qirbas: one qirba, and he used to protect their valley for them. When it was the time of ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), he appointed Sufyan ibn ‘Abdullah al-Thaqafi over them, and they refused to give him anything from the honey. So he wrote to ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) about that, and ‘Umar wrote to him: 'Indeed, bees are flying creatures of rain that Allah sends to whom He wills. If they give you what they used to give the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), then protect their valley for them; otherwise, leave between them and the people.' So they then paid him the tithe from it. Mentioned in al-Nihayah. And the meaning in it is that bees eat from the blossoms of trees and from their fruits, as Allah Almighty said: 'Then eat from all the fruits' (al-Nahl 16:69). And honey is produced from fruits, and in fruits if they are on tithe land: there is one-tenth, so likewise what is produced from them. But if the land is kharaj land, nothing is obligatory on it because its fruits do not have a tithe. And by this it differs from silkworms: for they eat leaves, not fruits, and there is nothing on leaves, so likewise what is produced from them, and what is produced from silkworms is silk, and there is no tithe on it due to what we mentioned. Then according to Abu Hanifa, the tithe is obligatory in honey, little or much, because it is analogous to fruits, and the tithe according to him is obligatory on little and much of fruits because the nisab is not considered in them. * His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said: There is nothing on it until it reaches ten ziqaq), each ziq: fifty mann, total: five hundred mann. His statement: (And Muhammad said: Five afraq, and the farq is thirty-six ratls by the Iraqi measure). The farq with two fathahs: a vessel that holds sixteen ratls. Mentioned in al-Mustasfa, and the muhaddithun make the ra' silent.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of zakat on honey, beginning with a general statement that one-tenth is due regardless of quantity when the honey is from tithe land. The commentator then provides a hadith proof from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Caliph ‘Umar, establishing that honey is subject to zakat. The reasoning is that bees feed on blossoms and fruits, and honey is a derivative of fruits; since fruits on tithe land incur the tithe, so does honey. However, if the land is kharaj (taxed) land, no tithe is owed because the fruits themselves are not tithed. The text distinguishes honey from silk: silkworms eat leaves (not fruits), and leaves incur no tithe, so silk is exempt. Following this, the passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute over the minimum amount (nisab) for honey. Abu Hanifa holds that the tithe is due on any amount, little or much, analogizing honey to fruits which have no nisab. Abu Yusuf requires the amount to reach ten ziqaq (five hundred mann), while Muhammad requires five afraq (a total of one hundred eighty ratls or about 540 pounds). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, that no minimum quantity is needed, although some later scholars apply a minimum of ten mann for practicality.

Key Terms
العشر (al-ushr): One-tenth (10%) tax on produce from tithe land (ard al-ushr) according to the Hanafi school.
زق (ziqq): A large waterskin used as a unit of measurement; one ziq equals fifty mann.
فرق (farq): A measure equal to sixteen ratls (Iraqi) or thirty-six ratls according to another interpretation; used by Muhammad for the nisab of honey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Five mann
B) Ten ziqaq
C) There is no minimum; any amount is subject to zakat
D) Five afraq

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that honey from tithe land is subject to ushr on any quantity, though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad set minimum thresholds.

Zakat on Honey: Nisab Dispute Among Hanafi Imams
Ruling on zakat of honey with intra-Hanafi dispute on nisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the nisab for zakat on honey and explain the qiyas that underlies Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
Honey is subject to 'ushr by qiyas to fruits, but the three Hanafi imams differ on whether a nisab is required.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents the rulings on zakat for honey within the Hanafi school. While all agree that honey is subject to 'ushr because it is derived from fruits, a significant intra-school dispute arises regarding the minimum amount (nisab) that triggers the obligation. The passage details the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad, along with the measurements they use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying qiyas
Understand how the author analogizes honey to fruits: honey is 'generated from fruits' (متولد من الثمار), so it follows the ruling of fruits – 'ushr on 'ushr land, nothing on kharaj land.
This qiyas is the foundation for the entire discussion.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ushr is obligatory on honey regardless of quantity because he does not consider nisab for fruits. His dalil is the direct qiyas to fruits.
Abu Hanifa views honey as essentially a fruit product.
3
State the positions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
Abu Yusuf requires a nisab of 10 azqiq (each zirqa = 50 mann, total 500 mann). Muhammad requires a nisab of 5 afraq (each farq = 36 Iraqi ratls). Their dalil is that honey is stored produce and should have a nisab like other zakatable items.
The measurements are explained in the commentary.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, any amount of honey triggers 'ushr; under the Sahibayn, honey below the nisab is exempt.
This affects small beekeepers differently.
5
Note the tarjih
The passage does not specify the mufta bihi, but later Hanafi practice often adopts the Sahibayn's requirement of a nisab.
This shows the evolution of the school's operative ruling.

وقال أبو يوسف : لا شيء فيه حتى يبلغ عشرة أزقاق .
وقال محمد : خمسة أفراق .

Chapter of zakat of crops and fruits. Abu Yusuf said: Nothing is due in it until it reaches ten azqiq. Muhammad said: Five afraq. And al-farq is thirty-six ratls by Iraqi measure. And honey is generated from fruits, and for fruits if they are on 'ushr land: one-tenth, so likewise what is generated from them. And if the land is kharaji: nothing is obligatory in it because its fruits have no 'ushr on them. And by this it differs from silkworms: because it eats leaves, not fruits, and on leaves there is nothing, so likewise what is generated from them, and what is generated from silkworms is silk (ibrisam), and there is no 'ushr on it for the reason we mentioned. Then according to Abu Hanifa, 'ushr is obligatory in honey, little or much, because it runs in the course of fruits, and 'ushr according to him is obligatory in little fruits and much, because nisab is not considered in them. * His saying: (Abu Yusuf said: Nothing in it until it reaches ten azqiq), each zirqa is fifty mann, and its total is five hundred mann. His saying: (And Muhammad said: Five afraq, and al-farq is thirty-six ratls by the Iraqi). Al-farq (with fath on f and ra): a vessel that takes sixteen ratls. Thus in al-Mustasfa, and the hadith scholars put sukun on the ra.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents intra-Hanafi dispute on the nisab for zakat on honey. The base ruling is that honey is subject to 'ushr because it is derived from fruits, and fruits from 'ushr land require 'ushr. By analogy (qiyas), honey should also require 'ushr. However, the imams differ on the minimum amount. Abu Hanifa holds that any quantity of honey requires 'ushr, just as with fruits, because nisab is not a condition for fruits according to him. Abu Yusuf sets a nisab of 10 azqiq (each zirqa = 50 mann, total 500 mann). Muhammad sets a nisab of 5 afraq (each farq = 36 Iraqi ratls). The commentator explains the measurements: a zirqa is a large vessel, a farq is a smaller measure. The passage also distinguishes honey from silk: silkworms eat leaves, which have no zakat, so their product (silk) has no 'ushr. The commentary clarifies that the farq used by Muhammad is a measure of capacity (16 ratls), while the text defines the farq weight as 36 ratls; the hadith scholars pronounce it with sukun on the ra.

Key Terms
الزق (zirqa): A unit of measurement for honey, equivalent to 50 mann (total 500 mann for 10 zirqa) as per the commentary.
الفرق (farq): A unit of volume; according to the commentary, it is a vessel that holds 16 ratls, but the matn defines it as 36 ratls by weight.
العشر ('ushr): The one-tenth zakat due on agricultural produce from 'ushr land.

No Zakat on Produce from Kharaj Land
Ruling statement with expansion on types of produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr for produce from kharaj land and identify the types of produce covered by the exemption.

Core Idea
Produce from kharaj land is exempt from 'ushr; double taxation is prevented.

This lesson addresses a specific exemption in zakat law: crops and honey from land that is subject to the kharaj tax are not subject to 'ushr (the one-tenth zakat on agricultural produce). The passage clarifies that this applies to all produce, including grains, fruits, and honey. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying zakat rules according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that there is no 'ushr on what comes out of kharaj land. So the ruling is that 'ushr is not due.
2
Recognize the type of land
Kharaj land is land conquered by force and subject to a land tax. This is distinct from 'ushr land.
3
Note the types of produce included
The commentator notes that the ruling may refer to honey, grains, and fruits. So all produce from such land is exempt.
4
Understand the rationale
The underlying principle is that kharaj and 'ushr do not combine. The land tax suffices, and no additional zakat on crops is imposed.
This prevents double taxation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس في الخارج من أرض الخراج عشر.

And there is no 'ushr on what comes out of kharaj land. * His saying: (And there is no 'ushr on what comes out of kharaj land). It may refer to what comes out of it from honey, and it may refer to grains and fruits, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a concise ruling that produce from kharaj land (land conquered by force and subject to tax) is not subject to 'ushr (the one-tenth zakat). The commentator notes that this applies to honey as well as grains and fruits. The rationale is that the land itself is subject to kharaj tax, and the produce is not additionally burdened with 'ushr. This distinguishes it from 'ushr land (land voluntarily cultivated by Muslims) where 'ushr is due. The ruling prevents double taxation and is based on the legal principle that kharaj and 'ushr do not combine.

Key Terms
أرض الخراج (ard al-kharaj): Land that is subject to kharaj tax, typically conquered lands that remain under the state's ownership.

No 'Ushr on Kharaj Land Produce
Ruling on zakat exemption for kharaj land produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding 'ushr on kharaj land produce and identify the types of produce included in the exemption.

Core Idea
Kharaj land produce is exempt from 'ushr; the land tax replaces the tithe.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that agricultural produce from kharaj land is not subject to the 'ushr (tithe) zakat. The text from al-Quduri is a clear ruling statement, and the commentary explores its scope, including whether it covers honey or only grains and fruits. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying zakat correctly to different land types in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the production of crops or fruits from kharaj land. The ruling is that no 'ushr is due on such produce.
The ruling is an exemption from a normally wajib payment.
2
Understand kharaj land
Kharaj land is land subject to a fixed tax (kharaj), typically conquered land left in non-Muslim hands. This tax replaces the 'ushr.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'ushr land and kharaj land; both are not combined.
3
Analyze the ambiguity in the commentary
The commentary notes that the exemption may apply to honey or to grains and fruits. This highlights a scholarly discussion on the scope of the term 'produce'.
The text does not resolve this ambiguity; it leaves it open.
4
Relate to the nisab principle
The commentary mentions that the nisab for 'ushr is five awsuq, based on the principle of taking five times the highest measure. This is the threshold for 'ushr on 'ushr land.
The nisab does not apply to kharaj land produce because it is exempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الزروع والثمار

وليس في الخارج من أرضِ الخَرَاج عُشر.
وإنما اعتبره بخمسة أفراق على أصله في اعتبار خمسة أمثال أعلى ما يُقدر به نوعه. * قوله: (وليس في الخارج من أرض الخراج : عشر). يحتمل أن يرجع إلى ما يخرج منها من العسل، ويحتمل من الحبوب والثمار، والله أعلم.
Chapter of Zakat on Crops and Fruits. And there is no 'ushr on what comes out of kharaj land. And he only considered it with five awsuq based on his principle in considering five times the highest of what its type is measured by. * His statement: (And there is no 'ushr on what comes out of kharaj land). It is possible that it refers to honey that comes out of it, and possible to grains and fruits, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the exemption of produce from kharaj land from the 'ushr (tithe) tax. The passage clarifies that the owner of kharaj land does not owe 'ushr on the crops or fruits grown on it, regardless of the type. The commentator explains the basis for the ruling: the nisab for 'ushr is five awsuq (a measure of volume), and this is derived from the principle that the nisab should be five times the highest measure by which the type is quantified. There is ambiguity whether the exemption applies to honey or to grains and fruits; the text leaves this as a matter of scholarly interpretation. The Hanafi school firmly holds that kharaj land is subject to a fixed land tax (kharaj) and is thereby exempt from 'ushr, because the two taxes are not combined on the same land.

Key Terms
أرض الخراج (ard al-kharāj): Land that is subject to the kharaj tax, typically conquered land left in the hands of non-Muslims or land subject to a fixed annual levy.
عشر (ʻushr): One-tenth of agricultural produce paid as zakat on land that is not subject to kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is subject to 'ushr if it reaches nisab.
B) It is not subject to 'ushr at all.
C) It is subject to both kharaj and 'ushr.
D) It is subject to 'ushr only if it is honey.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts produce from kharaj land from 'ushr, as the kharaj tax replaces the tithe on such land.

Zakat Recipients: Permissibility to Give All to One Category
Interpretation of Quran 9:60 on zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distributing zakat to the eight categories and explain the linguistic basis (lām) for this permissibility.

Core Idea
The lām in Quran 9:60 clarifies whom zakat may be given to, not that it must be divided among all categories.

This passage addresses a fundamental question in zakat fiqh: must zakat be distributed among all eight categories mentioned in the Quran? The Hanafi school, relying on a subtle linguistic analysis of the verse, holds that it is permissible to give all zakat to a single category or even a single individual. Understanding the difference between a lām of bayān and a lām of tamlik is essential for correctly applying this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the disbursement of zakat (obligatory charity). The ruling is permissibility (yajuz) to give all zakat to one of the eight categories or to one individual within a category.
The ruling is mubah (permissible), not wajib (obligatory) to distribute broadly.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 9:60, specifically the phrase 'li al-fuqarā'' and similar constructions for each category. The lām (li) is the key linguistic element.
The verse is qaṭī al-thubut (certain transmission) but ẓannī al-dalāla (ambiguous meaning).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah
The Hanafis interpret the lām as lām al-bayān (clarification of entitlement), not lām al-tashrīk (sharing/division). This means the verse only specifies who is eligible, not that each must receive a share.
No distributive particle (e.g., 'min' or 'ka') appears in the verse, supporting this interpretation.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
The Shāfiʿī school interprets the lām as lām al-tamlik (ownership), implying that each category owns a portion of the zakat fund, thus requiring distribution.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf rooted in usul al-fiqh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjīḥ
The Hanafi position is the muftā bihī (operative ruling) in the school, supported by the authority of the matn of al-Qudurī and the reasoning that each category is vast, so giving to one individual does not exclude the category.
The commentator emphasizes that the lām is for bayān, and the permissibility is explicit in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يجوز دفع الصدقة إليه، ومن لا يجوز

قال الله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَالْعَامِلِينَ عَلَيْهَا وَالْمُؤَلَّفَةِ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَفِي الرِّقَابِ وَالْغَارِمِينَ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ فَرِيضَةً مِنَ اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ عَلِيمٌ حَكِيمٌ﴾ [التوبة: 60].

اللام في هذا الباب لبيان جهة المستحق، لا للتشريك والقسمة.
بل كل صنف مما ذكرهم الله يجوز للإنسان دفع صدقته كلها إليه، دون بقية الأصناف.
ويجوز إلى واحد من الصنف؛ لأن كل صنف منهم لا يُحصى.
Chapter: On who it is permissible to give charity to, and who it is not permissible. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor, the needy, the workers over them, those whose hearts are reconciled, in freeing necks, the debtors, in the path of Allah, and the wayfarer— an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise.' [At-Tawbah: 60]. The lām in this chapter indicates the direction of the deserving one, not for sharing and division. Rather, every category that Allah mentioned, it is permissible for a person to give all of his charity to him, excluding the other categories. And it is permissible to give to one individual of the category, because every category of them is uncountable.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the disbursement of zakat, quoting Quran 9:60. The commentary explains the legal interpretation of the lām (preposition 'li') in the verse. The lām here is for bayān (clarification of the deserving categories), not for tashrīk (partnership) and qisma (division). This means that the eight categories mentioned are the types of people entitled to receive zakat, but it is not obligatory to distribute the zakat among all eight. It is permissible to give all the zakat to a single category and even to a single individual within that category. The reasoning is that each category is vast and uncountable, so giving to one individual does not violate the purpose. This is the established Hanafi position. The commentator also notes that the chapter is introduced because zakat must have its recipients (masārif).

Key Terms
الصدقات (al-ṣadaqāt): In this context, the obligatory zakat (alms) that is due on wealth.
لام (lām): The preposition 'li' in the verse, interpreted by Hanafis as indicating the direction of entitlement (bayān al-istihqāq), not a requirement to give to every category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) That the categories are options for the payer to choose from.
C) That all zakat must be given to the poor.
D) That the lām is for partnership and division.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving all zakat to one of the eight categories or even one individual, based on the interpretation of the lām as bayān, not tashrīk.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Permissibility of Giving All Zakat to One Recipient Category
Commentary on Quranic verse defining zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on concentrating zakat on one recipient category or individual and explain the linguistic proof from Surah At-Tawbah 9:60.

Core Idea
Zakat may be given to one category or even one individual — the verse's 'lam' indicates direction, not mandatory division.

When someone owes zakat, they must distribute it to one or more of the eight categories specified in the Quran. A common question is whether the zakat must be divided among all eight categories or can be given entirely to one. This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah presents the Hanafi view, based on a precise reading of the Quranic text, that concentration is permissible and sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the distribution of zakat: may a person give all their zakat to a single recipient category or even a single individual? The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz).
This differs from the common perception that all eight categories must receive a share.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Quranic verse 9:60. Identify the key words used: 'innama', 'lam', and 'fee'. These are the linguistic tools that yield the ruling.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (open to interpretation).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the Hanafi position? The word 'innama' restricts zakat exclusively to these eight categories—they are the only channels. The preposition 'lam' does not imply ownership or required division; rather, it indicates the direction of entitlement (li-bayan al-jihah). Therefore, giving to any one direction suffices.
The Tigris River analogy: swearing not to drink its water is broken by one gulp, because the genus is water, not the entire river.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools, especially the Shafi'is, interpret the 'lam' as indicating ownership (tamlik) and partnership (tashrik), which would require distribution among all eight categories. The Hanafis hold a different linguistic analysis.
The shift from 'lam' to 'fee' in the last four categories is used by Hanafis to argue that those categories are even more entitled, but the principle of permissibility stands for all.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the school, as established by al-Quduri and followed in Zahir al-Riwayah. It is a legitimate ikhtilaf with both sides having strong proofs.
The practical consequence is flexibility: a donor may choose to give all zakat to the most deserving category or even a single individual in dire need.

Chapter on who may be given charity and who may not. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, the charities are for the poor, the needy, those employed to collect them, those whose hearts are to be reconciled, for freeing necks, for those in debt, in the way of Allah, and the wayfarer – a duty from Allah, and Allah is All-Knowing, All-Wise' (At-Tawbah 9:60). When he mentioned zakat with its categories, and it must have its channels of disbursement, he presented the chapter on the channel. He (the author) said: Allah Almighty said ... (the verse). The preposition 'lam' in this chapter is to indicate the direction of the entitled recipient, not for partnership and division. Rather, every category that Allah mentioned, it is permissible for a person to give all of his charity to it, excluding the rest of the categories. And it is permissible to give to one individual of the category, because every category of them is uncountable, and attribution to that which is uncountable is not for ownership, but rather it is to indicate the direction, so it applies to the genus, which is the one individual. Do you not see that if someone swears not to drink the water of the Tigris, and then drinks one gulp of it, he breaks his oath, because he cannot drink all of it. So it is known that these eight categories as a whole are for zakat, like the Kaaba is for prayer, and each category of them is like a part of the Kaaba, and facing a part of the Kaaba is sufficient. His statement 'Indeed' is for affirming what is mentioned and negating what is other than it, and it is for the genus of charities upon these enumerated categories, and that they are specific to them, confined to them, as if He said: 'Indeed they are for them, and not for others.' His word 'the verse' in the nominative and accusative: 'hada' – the nominative on the assumption of 'the verse in its entirety', and the accusative on the assumption of 'complete the verse'. And He turned from 'lam' to 'fee' in the last four, to indicate that they are more firmly entitled to charity than those previously mentioned, because 'fee' indicates enclosure. And the repetition of 'fee' in His statement 'and in the way of Allah and the wayfarer' indicates the preference of these two over freeing necks and those in debt.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Quranic verse (9:60) that specifies the eight categories of zakat recipients. The author begins by quoting the verse, then explains the meaning of the preposition 'lam' in the verse. He clarifies that in this context, 'lam' does not imply partnership or required distribution among all categories, but rather indicates the direction or entitlement of the recipients. Therefore, it is permissible for a person to give all of his zakat to a single category (e.g., all to the poor) without dividing it among all eight. Furthermore, it is permissible to give zakat to just one individual within a category, because each category is vast and cannot be counted; when something is attributed to an uncountable group, it refers to the genus (jins), and a single individual represents that genus. He supports this with an analogy: if someone swears not to drink water from the Tigris River, drinking one gulp breaks the oath because he cannot drink all the water. Similarly, giving to one individual fulfills the obligation to the category. He then compares the eight categories to the Kaaba: as prayer is valid by facing any part of the Kaaba, so zakat is valid by giving to any one category. The word 'innama' (indeed) restricts zakat exclusively to these eight categories. He also discusses the shift from 'lam' to 'fee' in the last four categories (freeing necks, debtors, way of Allah, wayfarer) to emphasize their stronger entitlement and the repetition of 'fee' for the last two indicates their preference over the previous two. This is a standard Hanafi interpretation that allows flexibility in zakat distribution while maintaining the restriction to the eight specified categories.

Key Terms
الصدقات (al-sadaqat): The mandated zakat (obligatory charity) mentioned in the verse, specifically the eight categories.
اللام (al-lam): The preposition 'lam' in the verse is interpreted here as 'li-bayan al-jihah' (to indicate the direction of entitlement), not for 'tashrik' (partnership) or 'qismah' (division).
في (fee): The preposition 'fee' in the last four categories indicates enclosure, suggesting stronger entitlement than the categories introduced with 'lam'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not valid; zakat must be distributed among all eight categories.
B) It is permissible because each category is like a genus, and giving to one individual suffices.
C) It is only permissible if that person is a poor relative.
D) It is makruh (disliked) to give all zakat to one person.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat may be given entirely to one of the eight categories or even to a single individual within that category, based on the linguistic interpretation of the Quranic verse.

The Eight Zakat Categories and the Abrogation of 'Reconciled Hearts'
Explanation of the eight zakat categories and their abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight categories of zakat recipients from Quran 9:60, explain the Hanafi ruling that the category of 'reconciled hearts' is abrogated after the Prophet, and apply the principle that a ruling ceases when its reason (illa) ceases.

Core Idea
The reason for giving zakat to reconcile hearts ceased when Islam became strong, so the ruling also ceased.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the eight categories of zakat recipients as mentioned in the Quran. The author clarifies the grammatical nuance of the prepositions used for different categories, indicating varying degrees of deservingness. The key ruling discussed is that the category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum) no longer receives zakat after the death of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), because the underlying reason for its existence—the weakness of Islam—has disappeared.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight categories
List the eight categories from Quran 9:60 that are mentioned in the text: the poor, the needy, those employed to collect zakat, those whose hearts are to be reconciled, slaves, those in debt, in the way of Allah, and the traveler.
These are the only valid recipients of zakat.
2
Understand the grammatical nuance
Distinguish between the preposition 'lam' (ownership) for the first four categories and 'fi' (containment) for the last four. The text notes that 'fi' indicates a stronger deservingness, especially for 'in the way of Allah' and 'the traveler'.
This nuance affects how we understand the recipients' relationship to the zakat funds.
3
Recognize the dropping of a category
The text explicitly states that 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' has been dropped from the list after the time of the Prophet.
This is a change in ruling based on a change in circumstances.
4
Analyze the reason (illa)
The text provides the reason: 'because Allah strengthened Islam and made it independent of them' (لأن الله تعالى أعز الإسلام، وأغنى عنهم). This is the 'illa' for the original ruling.
The cause for giving them zakat was the weakness of Islam and the need to attract or pacify people.
5
Apply the talil principle
When the 'illa' ceases, the ruling (giving zakat to this category) ceases as well. This is a fundamental Hanafi legal principle: rulings are contingent on their effective cause.
Thus, after Islam became strong, the ruling was abrogated, not the Quranic verse but its applicability.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the eight categories of zakat recipients from the Quran (9:60). The author begins by clarifying a grammatical point: when the verse says 'for the poor and needy...' the preposition 'lam' indicates ownership, but when it says 'in the way of Allah' and 'the son of the road' the preposition 'fi' is used, which signifies that these two categories are more firmly deserving because 'fi' implies inclusion. The author then states that these eight categories are exhaustive for zakat distribution, just as the Kaaba is the direction for prayer; it is sufficient to face a part of it. The commentary then notes that the category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum) has dropped from the list after the Prophet's time because Allah strengthened Islam and made it independent of them. The author explains the three types of such people who were given zakat during the Prophet's life: (1) those given to convert them and their people, (2) those who were weak in faith to be strengthened, (3) those given to avoid their harm, citing examples like 'Abbas ibn Mirdas, 'Uyayna ibn Hisn, etc. The Prophet gave them not out of fear but to prevent them from being cast into Hell. The passage answers a potential objection: how could zakat be given to non-Muslims? The response is that at that time, jihad was obligatory on all Muslims, and giving them this share was like a substitute for jihad; then after the Prophet's death, this share abrogated because the reason (jihad) changed.

Key Terms
المؤلفة قلوبهم (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled; non-Muslims or weak Muslims given zakat to incline them to Islam or avoid their harm.
في (fi): A preposition indicating containment, used for the last four categories to emphasize stronger deservingness.
اللام (al-lam): A preposition indicating ownership, used for the first four categories of zakat recipients.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi school rule that the category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' no longer receives zakat?
A) Because the Prophet forbade it after his death.
B) Because Allah strengthened Islam and made it independent of them.
C) Because there are no more non-Muslims.
D) Because the Quran only mentioned eight categories and this one was not included.

Key Takeaway
The category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' no longer applies because the reason for it—the weakness of Islam—has been removed after the Prophet.

Omission of Author's Heart Category and Definitions of Poor and Needy
Explains omission and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the category of 'al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum' is no longer eligible for zakat and distinguish between faqir and miskin as defined by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Consensus ended the author's heart category; faqir does not beg, miskin does.

Zakat has eight specified recipients in the Quran, but one category—those whose hearts are to be reconciled—has been omitted by consensus after the Prophet's death. This passage from Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyirah explains the historical basis for that omission and then clarifies the Hanafi definitions of the poor (faqir) and the needy (miskin), along with a subtle point about their priority order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Omitted Category
The passage states that the category 'al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum' has fallen from the eight. Identify the three subtypes that existed during the Prophet's time.
These subtypes were to attract non-Muslims, strengthen weak faith, and prevent harm.
2
Understand the Reason for Omission
The omission is based on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions after the Prophet's death, as Islam became strong. Note the actions of Abu Bakr and Umar that confirmed this.
The passage recounts that Umar tore the document and declared Islam independent of them.
3
Distinguish Faqir and Miskin
According to the Hanafi school, faqir is one who possesses at least something but does not beg, while miskin is one who has nothing and begs. Recognize the key differentiator: asking or not asking.
The source cites 'al-Yanabi' for this definition.
4
Resolve the Priority Question
The Quran mentions faqir before miskin, though miskin seems more needy. The passage explains that faqir is given priority because he does not ask, so he is more deserving of attention. However, this distinction has no practical effect in zakat distribution.
Both are eligible, and the difference in priority does not change permissibility.

Chapter on who is permissible to give charity to, and who is not. So these are eight categories. And from them has fallen the category of those whose hearts are reconciled because Allah Almighty has glorified Islam and made independent of them. And they are three types: 1- A type that the Prophet used to reconcile to become Muslims, and their people would become Muslim by their Islam. 2- And a type among them who became Muslim but with weakness, so he wanted to confirm them in it. And a type he gave to ward off their evil, like Abbas ibn Mirdas al-Sulami, Uyayna ibn Hisn al-Fazari, Safwan ibn Umayya al-Qurashi, al-Aqra' ibn Habis al-Tamimi, and Abu Sufyan ibn Harb al-Umawi. The Messenger of Allah did not give them out of fear of them; the Prophets, peace be upon them, do not fear anyone except Allah, but he gave them out of fear that Allah would throw them on their faces into the fire of Hell. If it is said: How is it permissible to give to them while they are disbelievers? It is said: Because jihad is obligatory upon the poor and rich Muslims, so giving to them from the wealth of the poor was in place of their jihad at that time, as if he gave it to them. Then this share fell with the death of the Messenger of Allah. When the Messenger of Allah died, the reconciled ones came to Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, and asked him to write for them according to their custom. So he wrote for them, and they took the document to Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, to get his signature on the sheet. He tore it up and said: 'We have no need of you; Allah has glorified Islam and made independent of you. Either you become Muslim, or else the sword is between us and you.' So they returned to Abu Bakr and said: 'Are you the caliph or is he?' He said: 'He, if Allah wills, and he carried out what Umar did.' His statement: 'And from them has fallen the reconciled ones' because consensus was reached on that. His statement: 'And the poor is one who has the least thing, and the needy is one who has nothing.' He said in 'al-Yanabi': The poor is one who does not ask people nor goes around doors, and the needy is one who asks people and goes around doors. And this difference does not yield any benefit in zakat because it is permissible to give to
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyirah is a commentary on the chapter of zakat recipients. It begins by noting that the Quranic eight categories (Surah At-Tawbah: 60) have been reduced in practice to seven, as the category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum) is no longer applicable. The commentator explains that this category included three types: (1) non-Muslims given zakat to attract them and their people to Islam, (2) new Muslims with weak faith to strengthen them, and (3) individuals given to prevent their harm. The Prophet used to give them not out of fear but out of mercy to save them from Hell. After the Prophet's death, the caliphs Abu Bakr and Umar refused to continue this practice, and consensus (ijma') was established that this category is no longer eligible. The passage then defines 'faqir' (poor) as one who has some property but does not beg, and 'miskin' (needy) as one who has nothing and begs. A subtle point is raised: why is faqir mentioned first in the Quran, even though miskin is more needy? The answer is that faqir does not ask, so they deserve priority; but in zakat distribution, both are eligible and it does not affect the ruling.

Key Terms
المؤلفة قلوبهم (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled; a category of zakat recipients who were given sadaqah to incline them to Islam, strengthen their faith, or prevent their harm.
الفقير (al-faqir): According to the passage, the one who has the least thing (i.e., some property but insufficient) and does not beg or go door-to-door.
المسكين (al-miskin): According to the passage, the one who has nothing and begs or goes door-to-door.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the Prophet ordered its removal before his death

Key Takeaway
The category of 'al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum' is no longer a valid zakat recipient due to consensus, and the Hanafi definitions of faqir and miskin are based on whether the person begs or not.

The Removal of al-Mu'allafah from Zakat Recipients
Evidence for the removal of al-mu'allafah from zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the exclusion of al-mu'allafah from zakat recipients and explain the consensus (ijma) proof used to support it.

Core Idea
The category of 'those whose hearts are reconciled' is permanently removed from zakat by the consensus of the Companions.

This passage deals with a historical change in zakat distribution. The commentator explains that the category of al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum (those whose hearts are reconciled) has been dropped from the eight categories of zakat recipients. The proof is the consensus of the Companions, as demonstrated by the incident involving Abu Bakr and Umar after the Prophet's death.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon (giving zakat to al-mu'allafah) and its hukm (invalid).
The passage begins with 'قوله : وقد سقط منها المؤلّفة' indicating the removal.
2
Identify the proof
Locate the dalil cited: the consensus of the Companions, illustrated by the story.
The commentator says 'لأن الإجماع انعقد على ذلك'.
3
Trace the evidence
Analyze how the story proves the consensus: Abu Bakr's initial writing, Umar's objection, and Abu Bakr's approval.
The narrative shows agreement of the two leading Companions, representing wider consensus.
4
Note the implication
Determine the practical effect: zakat cannot be given to al-mu'allafah; if given, the obligation is not fulfilled.
This ruling is binding in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وقد سقط منها المؤلّفة: لأن الإجماع انعقد على ذلك. «فلما مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم جاءت المؤلفة إلى أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه، وطلبوا منه أن يكتب لهم بعادتهم: فكتب لهم، فذهبوا بالكتاب إلى عمر رضي الله عنه ليأخذوا خطّه على الصحيفة: فمزقها، وقال : لا حاجة لنا بكم، فقد أعزّ الله الإسلام، وأغنى عنكم، إما أسلمتم وإلا فالسيف بيننا وبينكم. فرجعوا إلى أبي بكر، فقالوا له : أنت الخليفة، أم هو؟ فقال : هو إن شاء الله، وأمضى ما فعله عمر رضي الله عنه.»
He said: 'And the 'those whose hearts are reconciled' have been dropped from it because consensus was established on that.' 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died, the Mu'allafa came to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) and asked him to write for them according to their custom. So he wrote for them. They took the document to Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) to get his signature on the paper. He tore it and said: We have no need of you. Allah has exalted Islam and made us independent of you. Either you accept Islam, or the sword is between us and you. So they returned to Abu Bakr and said: Are you the caliph or is he? He said: He is, Allah willing, and he approved what Umar had done (may Allah be pleased with him).'
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The commentator begins by stating the ruling: the category of al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum (those whose hearts are to be reconciled) has been removed from the eight categories of zakat recipients. The proof is the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, demonstrated by the historical incident. After the Prophet's death, the Mu'allafa came to Abu Bakr asking for their share, as was the practice during the Prophet's lifetime. Abu Bakr initially wrote for them, but Umar objected, tore the document, and declared that Islam no longer needed them. Abu Bakr then agreed with Umar, establishing the consensus that this category was no longer applicable. This ruling is binding and reflects the Hanafi position that the Mu'allafa are not eligible for zakat.

Key Terms
المؤلفة (al-mu'allafah): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled, a category of zakat recipients whose share was discontinued by consensus after the death of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Companions reached consensus that Islam no longer needed to win their hearts.
D) Because the Quranic verses were abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The category of 'those whose hearts are reconciled' is no longer eligible for zakat due to the consensus of the Companions.
